  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

        state: 'apple_oauth_state_789aef03-9bd1-4526-8a0a-559f18312621'

<a href="/questions/519418-i-am-trying-to-find-good-read-aloud">I am trying to find good read aloud stories for high school students (ages 16-21). I&#39;m trying to read adult/teen books, but need somewhat simple language. The students are from pre-K to 2nd grade in reading level. I love the story &amp; graphics in this book. 

Does this seem like a good match?</a>
</div>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/7451212-stormcrow"><img alt="" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_100x100-259587f1619f5253426a4fa6fb508831.png" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/7451212-stormcrow">Stormcrow</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<div class='spoiler'>
This answer contains spoilers…
<span class='spoilerAnswerText'>
<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  
    I disagree with David. Although there certainly are plenty of literary references kids won't get, the book also has classic horror creatures that they<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">…more</a>
    I disagree with David. Although there certainly are plenty of literary references kids won't get, the book also has classic horror creatures that they'll instantly recognize (Dracula, Frankenstein, and the Wolf Man; not to mention Jack the Ripper and Sherlock Holmes). It may require some explaining and you might want to gloss over much of the chapter where they visit the dream world, but otherwise, I think this is a very enjoyable book for readers of any age. (Don't forget that just because their reading level is low, their comprehension as teenagers and young adults won't necessarily be.) Obviously, I'm late in answering your question and it's too far into October to read it now, but perhaps next year.<a href="#" rel="nofollow noopener">(less)</a>
  
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>
</span>
</div>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781556525605" href="/book/show/21470616-a-night-in-the-lonesome-october">review of another edition</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2739894232" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6857107670879759641"> I will probably quote something for each day just for shits n giggles! <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1600260980ra/30113968.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>October 1</b><br/><br/><b>
  <blockquote>MADE THE CIRCUITS. THE THING IN THE CIRCLE changed shape, finally making itself look like a lady dog of attractive person and very friendly disposition. But I was not fooled into breaking the Circle. It didn’t have the smell part down yet</blockquote>
</b><br/><br/><b>October 2</b><br/><br/><b>
  <blockquote>WE TOOK A WALK LAST NIGHT. ACQUIRING mandrake root in a field far from here at the place of a killing by somebody else. The master wrapped it in silk and took it to </blockquote></b></span>
  <span id="freeText6857107670879759641" style="display:none"> I will probably quote something for each day just for shits n giggles! <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1600260980ra/30113968.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>October 1</b><br><br><b>
  <blockquote>MADE THE CIRCUITS. THE THING IN THE CIRCLE changed shape, finally making itself look like a lady dog of attractive person and very friendly disposition. But I was not fooled into breaking the Circle. It didn’t have the smell part down yet</blockquote>
</b><br><br><b>October 2</b><br><br><b>
  <blockquote>WE TOOK A WALK LAST NIGHT. ACQUIRING mandrake root in a field far from here at the place of a killing by somebody else. The master wrapped it in silk and took it to his work space direct. I could hear him engage in good-natured banter with the Thing in the Circle. Jack has a long list of ingredients, and things must be done properly on schedule.</blockquote>
</b><br><br><b>October 3</b><br><br><b>
  <blockquote>WE WALKER AGAIN LAST NIGHT, AND THE master was hunting. He had donned his cloak and said to me, "Snuff, fetch!" And from the way he said it, I knew that it was the blade he required. I took it to him and we went out. Our luck was varied. That is, he obtained the ingredients he was after, but only with considerable turmoil and an inordinate passage of time. We were discovered near the end. I gave warning, and we had to flee. It was a long chase, till finally I hung back and nipped the other on the leg. We made good our escape, with the ingredients. As he was washing up later, Jack told me I was an excellent watchdog. I was very proud</blockquote>
</b> <br><br><b>October 4</b><br><br><b>
  <blockquote>RAINY DAY. WINDY, TOO. I MADE MY ROUNDS. <br>"Up yours, cur."<br>"Same to you."<br>"Hi, things."<br>Slither, slither. <br>"How’s about letting me out?"<br>"Nope"<br>"My day will come."<br>"Not today."<br>The usual. Everything seemed in order. <br>"How’s about a collie? You like redheads?"<br>"You still haven’t got it right. S'long."<br>"Son of a bitch!"</blockquote>
</b><br><br><b>October 5</b><br><br><b>
  <blockquote>I BREAKFASTED IN THE DARK AND MADE MY rounds of the house. Everything was in good order. The master was asleep so I let myself out and prowled the vicinity. The day would not begin for some time yet.</blockquote>
</b><br><br><b>October 6</b><br><br><b>
  <blockquote>EXCITEMENT. I HEARD THE MIRROR CRACK this morning, and I ran and raised holy hell before it, keeping the slithers inside. Jack heard the fuss and fetched the mundane wand and transferred them all to another mirror, just like the Yellow Emperor. This one was much smaller, which may teach them a lesson, but probably not. We’re not sure how they did it. Continued pressure on some flaw, most likely. Good thing they are afraid of me.</blockquote>
</b><br><br><b>October 7</b><br><br><b>
  <blockquote>WE WERE OUT AGAIN LAST NIGHT IN PURSUIT of more ingredients for the Great Work. It was very foggy, and there were many patrolman about. This did not stop us, but it made things more difficult. The master's blade flashed, the woman screamed, and there was a rending of garments. We passed the Great Detective in our flight, and I inadvertently tripped his companion, whose limp had lessened his ability to avoid onrushing canines.</blockquote>
</b><br><br><b>October 8</b><br><br><b>
  <blockquote>I DREW MORE LINES IN MY HEAD LAST NIGHT and this morning, but before I’d created a satisfactory picture we had a caller</blockquote>
</b><br><br><b>October 9</b><br><br><b>
  <blockquote>LAST NIGHT WE OBTAINED MORE INGREDIENTS for the master's spell. As we paused on a corner in Soho the Great Detective and his companion came out of the fog and approached us.</blockquote>
</b><br><br><b>October 10</b><br><br><b>
  <blockquote>The thing was strangely quiet as I entered the basement. In a moment, I saw why. We had developed a leak. The water entered at the wall, ran along a sagging beam, and dripped down several feet farther in. It had formed a puddle, and the puddle was slowly spreading. One moist pseudopod was extended in the direction of the Circle, having perhaps another ten inches to run before it breached it.</blockquote>
</b><br><br><b>October 11</b><br><br><b>
  <blockquote>A brisk morning. After I made my rounds I went outside. I could discover nothing untoward, so I set off in the direction of the Good Doctor’s place. As I was trotting along the road, however, I heard a familiar voice from a small grove to my right:</blockquote>
</b><br><br><b>October 12</b><br><br><b>
  <blockquote>Slow day. The Thing in the circle tried being a greyhound. I was never attracted to skinny ladies, though. Growled a few times at the Thing in the Attic. Watched the slitherers. Watched Jack as he puttered with the acquisitions. It was still too early for him actually to start using them.</blockquote>
</b><br><br><b>October 13</b><br><br><b>
  <blockquote>"Snuff! Let me in! Help!" it cried <br>It was Needle. <br>"I know better than to invite you guys inside," I said. <br>"That’s the boss! I’m just a bat! I don’t even like tomato juice! Please!"</blockquote>
</b><br><br><b>October 14</b><br><br><b>
  <blockquote>We approached. The birds were gone. So were the eyes. The man in uniform. His throat had been cut.</blockquote>
</b><br><br><b>October 15</b><br><br><b>
  <blockquote>I went and dragged the corpse til I couldn’t manage another step. Then I dragged myself home, jaws aching, paws sore, my old injury from the zombie affair was acting up.</blockquote>
</b><br><br><b>October 16</b><br><br><b>
  <blockquote>I made my way back to the body, which had a few more missing parts and didn’t smell too good, and dragged it to the next place of concealment.</blockquote>
</b><br><br><b>October 17</b><br><br><b>
  <blockquote>"Damn! I need a left femur and this one ain’t got one!"</blockquote>
</b><br><br><b>October 18</b><br><br><b>
  <blockquote>He loomed nearer. Monstrous jaws, great feral eyes. . . Then he sat down. <br>"So this is where it is," he said. <br>"What?"<br>"The missing body. Snuff, you are tampering with evidence."<br>"And you might say I’m tampering with something already tampered with. Who are you?"<br>"Larry. Talbot."<br>"Could’ve fooled me. I thought you were-a great wolf. . . oh."</blockquote>
</b><br><br><b>October 19</b><br><br><b>
  <blockquote>The Thing in the Streamer Trunk had poked a small hole in the front. An enormous yellow eye regarded me through it. It didn’t make a sound, though.</blockquote>
</b><br><br><b>October 20</b><br><br><b>
  <blockquote>There was a big fellow lurching about the place-drunk perhaps. Biggest man I’ve ever seen. He was only about for a little while, during the height of the storm. Then he lay down on that fancy bed in the basement, and the Good Doctor covered him up, entirely, with a sheet. He didn’t stir again.</blockquote>
</b><br><br><b>October 21</b><br><br><b>
  <blockquote>The things are getting restless, but their restraints still serve.</blockquote>
</b><br><br><b>October 22</b><br><br><b>
  <blockquote>"Come on!" it said. "I’m almost strong enough to break out of here on my own now. It won’t go well with you if you keep me til I do."<br>"'Almost,'" I said, "isn’t good enough."<br>It growled. I growled back. It flinched. I was still in control.</blockquote>
</b><br><br><b>October 23</b><br><br><b>
  <blockquote>Up in the morning, out on the job. I hassled the Things, then checked around outside. A black feather lay near the front door. Could be one of Nightwind’s. Could be openers on a nasty spell. Could be just a stray feather. I carried it across the road to the field and pissed on it.</blockquote>
</b><br><br><b>October 24</b><br><br><b>
  <blockquote>"I’ll invite you into the parlor," Jack said, "if you don’t mind stepping over a few dismembered ogres."<br>"Never did before," the lady answered, as he led her in that direction.</blockquote>
</b><br><br><b>October 25</b><br><br><b>
  <blockquote>Someone stuffed him into one of his baskets and torched it.</blockquote>
</b><br><br><b>October 26</b><br> <br><b>
  <blockquote>"What’s going on at the end of the month?"<br>"Weird stuff," I said. "A little specialized craziness. Stay away from any human gatherings that night."</blockquote>
</b><br><br><b>October 27</b><br><br><b>
  <blockquote>"'The experiment man'?"<br>"You know. The big fellow the Good Doctor put together from all the parts his assistant dig up for him."</blockquote>
</b><br><br><b>October 28</b><br><br><b>
  <blockquote>Mrs. Enderby happened to be in a tree in her yard with a pair of binoculars when I passed, and called out to me. <br>"Snuff, please come here!"<br>I kept going.</blockquote>
</b><br><br><b>October 29</b><br><br><b>
  <blockquote>Then I noticed a peculiar shape to the rear-that of a bat hanging from a beam. While all bats look pretty much alike to me, especially when you turn them upside-down, it reminded me a lot of Needle. I approached and said loudly, "Hey, Needle! What the hell are you doing here?"</blockquote>
</b><br><br><b>October 30</b><br><br><b>
  <blockquote>Players may fall, or go mad, catch fire, be transformed.</blockquote>
</b><br><br><b>October 31</b><br><br><b>
  <blockquote>Jack and Jill went down the hill. Gray and I ran after</blockquote>
</b><br><br>Happy Halloween 🎃 <br><br>•••••••••••••••<br><br>Thank you to my friends <b>Tadiana and Evgeny</b> for turning me on to this book and this author! I will be rereading this for October as each chapter is a day in October. I might summarize my feelings during the whole process. <br><br><img src="https://s3.amazonaws.com/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1551834579r/27160420.gif?v=1551834587738" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Mel 🖤🐶🐺🐾</span>
  <a data-text-id="6857107670879759641" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_756506537" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/756506537" />
    <a title="Evgeny" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9340136-evgeny"><img alt="Evgeny" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1544797852p2/9340136.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/756506537?book_show_action=true">Nov 01, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Evgeny" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Evgeny" href="/user/show/9340136-evgeny">Evgeny</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9340136-evgeny?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer756506537" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5318001488412941631"><b>Review updated yet again (and again and again) on November 1, 2020</b><br/><br/><b>A group read with some of my greatest friends: <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/3978225' rel='nofollow noopener'>Carol</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/7298986-sarah-former-nefarious-breeder-of-murderous-crustaceans' rel='nofollow noopener'>Sarah</a>. </b><br/><br/>First a disclaimer: I lost count to the number of times I read the book. Seriously. I still find something new with each reread. Just one example: only during my last reread I was able to see the connection between this book and Amber series (a shadow traveling bit). <br/><br/>The book is very quotable. In fact, we keep finding amusing quotes during our forth read we managed to</span>
  <span id="freeText5318001488412941631" style="display:none"><b>Review updated yet again (and again and again) on November 1, 2020</b><br><br><b>A group read with some of my greatest friends: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/3978225" rel="nofollow noopener">Carol</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/7298986-sarah-former-nefarious-breeder-of-murderous-crustaceans" rel="nofollow noopener">Sarah</a>. </b><br><br>First a disclaimer: I lost count to the number of times I read the book. Seriously. I still find something new with each reread. Just one example: only during my last reread I was able to see the connection between this book and Amber series (a shadow traveling bit). <br><br>The book is very quotable. In fact, we keep finding amusing quotes during our forth read we managed to overlook before. Just one example: <br><br><i>"I took Jack his slippers this evening and lay at his feet before a roaring fire while he smoked his pipe, sipped sherry, and read the newspaper. He read aloud everything involving killings, arsons, mutilations, grave robberies, church desecrations, and unusual thefts. It is very pleasant just being domestic sometimes."</i><br><br>Another one (sorry, I simply cannot resist):<br><br><i>"Never trust a cat, anyway. All they’re good for is stringing tennis racquets."</i><br><br>The most common cover of the book is so perfect I cannot help showing it here. <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/photos/1504061640p8/3617376.jpg" width="330" height="500" alt="Cover" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Half of the fun in most of Zelazny's books is to figure out what is going on. For this reason I have to be as obscure as possible. Imagine Jack the Ripper, Sherlock Holmes, Count Dracula, Dr. Frankenstein, Rasputin, Larry Talbot (if you do not know who he is, I am not giving a spoiler), and some other well-known and interesting characters gather in one place waiting for the Halloween night when they are supposed to do something. The tale is told from a dog's POV who for some reason reminds me of following:<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1509061489i/24288510._SX540_.jpg" alt="Sam" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Are you confused? Sorry, this is the best I can do. If you are really lost everything will be explained later in the book.<br><br>The tale is fairly lighthearted with quite a few jokes and puns, but when you stop to think about it, the plot is actually quite spooky. It takes a real master writer of Zelazny's caliber to make it work - and it does work, even when it seemingly goes over the top. The author pays homage to the creators of all of the characters I mentioned above as well as Poe, Bradbury, and Lovecraft (Cthulhu makes a brief appearance as well); I am sure I missed somebody.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1541118672i/26534995._SY540_.jpg" width="250" height="300" alt="Chtulhu" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>After I finished reading the book the first time I was wondering why in the world I have not read it earlier - several times. This exact question remained during my second read as well. In my first read after the initial confusion there came a moment when I realized I really do not want to put the book down. Fortunately, Zelazny was also the master of packing a lot of thoughts and plot movements into a very limited number of pages, so I still had several hours of much needed sleep left when I finished reading - going to bed before that was totally out of question. Only during my last reread I finally got enough sleep and only because we read one chapter a day (there are 31 chapters total) and the chapters are fairly short. It is safe to say the book became my traditional Halloween read. I am afraid at least one of my friends caught the came bug. Sorry. <br><br>In conclusion, if you are looking for a spooky Halloween read, look no further.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1478043583i/21024200._SX540_.jpg" alt="Grumpy Halloween" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Heck, if you are looking just for any good read, look no further as well. Just read the book. You will not regret it, but if you have not read it yet - you are missing a lot. <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1478043583i/21024201.jpg" alt="Halloween" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="5318001488412941631" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_179590200" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/179590200" />
    <a title="carol. " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3978225-carol"><img alt="carol. " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1307934801p2/3978225.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/179590200?book_show_action=true">Jun 25, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="carol. " class="user" itemprop="url" name="carol. " href="/user/show/3978225-carol">carol. </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">genre-defiers, October fans</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=awards">awards</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=classic">classic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=my-library-trade">my-library-trade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3978225-carol?shelf=fast-and-fun">fast-and-fun</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer179590200" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17587913096900322714">Zelazny is a genius... although I have a sneaking suspicion his genius may be drug related. Where else would you come up with the idea of telling a Victorian mystery-humor-horror story from the point of view of a dog?<br/><br/>The first clue of the kind of upcoming weirdness comes from the dedication to Shelley, Poe, Stoker, Doyle, Lovecraft, Bradbury, Bloch, and Terhune (dog breeder and writer). The the cast of characters include the watchdog Snuff, and his master, Jack, a man who is particularly talente</span>
  <span id="freeText17587913096900322714" style="display:none">Zelazny is a genius... although I have a sneaking suspicion his genius may be drug related. Where else would you come up with the idea of telling a Victorian mystery-humor-horror story from the point of view of a dog?<br /><br />The first clue of the kind of upcoming weirdness comes from the dedication to Shelley, Poe, Stoker, Doyle, Lovecraft, Bradbury, Bloch, and Terhune (dog breeder and writer). The the cast of characters include the watchdog Snuff, and his master, Jack, a man who is particularly talented with a knife, with support from a host of horror and mystery classics. The Great Detective and his sidekick are in the vicinity, investigating the sudden uptick in activity. The Count drops by in his flowing, dark glory. The Good Doctor has moved into a nearby farmhouse looking for some quiet space in which to conduct various experiments. Is it any surprise he has a misshapen dwarf sidekick and an experiment man? And perhaps, in the vein of Bloch, there's a bad pun or two--really, Zelazny, <i>really??</i><br /><br />Presented as the daily dairy of a mathematically-talented watchdog, Snuff, it describes the events as he and Jack prepare for a final confrontation on October 31. Spell and geographical preparations need to be made while strategizing against the other participants. I have to admire how Zelazny takes simple sentence structure to initially build believability in a dog narrator (although, to be fair, there are hints he might be more than canine), but by story end, he is at his usual level of sophistication and imagery. Actually, the sense-world of the canine rather lends itself to Zelazny's imagery.<br /><b><br />Streaks of high cirrus fluoresced above us from the stars they framed, and a gust of wind stirred my fur."<br /></b><br /><br />Underneath the spell-preparing graveyard shenanigans is the building of a potentially deadly conflict. Preparations make for strange bedfellows, and Snuff finds himself relying on Ms. Greymalk the cat. He also interacts with a variety of other animal companions to the primary, somewhat questionably human, players.<br /><br />Zelazny must have had a blast writing this. There's amusing variations on a theme wandering through the month. Notable are the many disguises of the Great Detective, and the variety of injuries his companion displays. There's a particularly fun ongoing riff using the Things that Jack and Snuff guard. The Things in the Mirror, Thing in the Wardrobe, the Thing in the Steamer Trunk and the Thing in the Circle downstairs are always trying to escape, but are kept under control by Snuff's ferociousness. The Thing in the Circle has settled for deception as its escape strategy, and daily turns into some type of dog, hoping to tempt Snuff.<br /><br /><b>"Down in the cellar the Thing in the Circle had become a Pekingese.<br />'You like little ladies?' it asked. "Come and get it, big fella.'<br />It still smelled of Thing rather than dog.<br />'You're not really very bright,' I said.<br />The Peke gave me the paw as I departed, and it's hard to turn your leg that way."</b><br /><br />I waver back and forth between four and five stars, but ultimately, anything that's read this fondly and wins a place in my library deserves five. My mild dissatisfaction comes from a section where Zelazny indulges in an ode to a Lovecraft short, 'The Cats of Ulthar,' which didn't seem to be particularly germane to the narrative and only connected best you knew the short.* What pushed me over the edge were the two puns at the end, of which the penultimate left me with fond groans.<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  <b>"Any port in a storm</b>
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />*Thanks to Evgeny<br /><br />Re-read 10/2019: I'm a bit ambivalent about the illustrations by Gahan Wilson. Wilson's style here reminds me of ink drawings for stain glass work, a sort of heavy block-print style, and just don't work for me. However, when I did a little researching on this book, it turns out that Zelazny envisioned the book with Wilson's illustrations since 1979. (<a href="https://lovecraftzine.com/magazine/issues/2012-2/issue-18-october-2012/fallen-books-and-other-subtle-clues-in-zelaznys-a-night-in-the-lonesome-october-by-dr-christopher-s-kovacs/" rel="nofollow noopener">source</a> but was only able to complete it in 1993, at the end of his life. As such, I suppose they belong together, but I far prefer the words to the text.<br /><br />Additional resource: <a href="https://middletownpubliclib.org/wp-content/uploads/2019/07/Roger-Zelazny-Panel-2.pdf" rel="nofollow noopener">Science Fiction Book Club<br />Interview with Dr. Christopher S. Kovacs and Warren Lapine September 2018 </a><br /><br />Cross posted at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://clsiewert.wordpress.com/2012/12/27/a-night-in-the-lonesome-october-by-roger-zelazny/">http://clsiewert.wordpress.com/2012/1...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="17587913096900322714" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_419438279" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/419438279" />
    <a title="Nataliya" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3672777-nataliya"><img alt="Nataliya" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605995014p2/3672777.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/419438279?book_show_action=true">Sep 21, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nataliya" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nataliya" href="/user/show/3672777-nataliya">Nataliya</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3672777-nataliya?shelf=2014-reads">2014-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3672777-nataliya?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3672777-nataliya?shelf=hugo-nebula">hugo-nebula</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3672777-nataliya?shelf=2019-reads">2019-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3672777-nataliya?shelf=2020-reads">2020-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer419438279" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6696659716175626955"><blockquote>
<i>"Carpe baculum!"</i> (Seize the stick!)</blockquote>You know the feeling when you finish the book and with a quiet satisfied and slightly smug smile realize that<b> it was just perfect</b>, as though it was written just for you? Sometimes I get lucky like that. <br/><br/>Roger Zelazny has a unique quirkiness in his narration that speaks directly to me, and <i>A Night in the Lonesome October</i> which I read in one breath over the wee hours of a late October night is no exception.<br/><br/>Zelazny is a genius when it comes to telling a story. Th</span>
  <span id="freeText6696659716175626955" style="display:none"><blockquote>
<i>"Carpe baculum!"</i> (Seize the stick!)</blockquote>You know the feeling when you finish the book and with a quiet satisfied and slightly smug smile realize that<b> it was just perfect</b>, as though it was written just for you? Sometimes I get lucky like that. <br><br>Roger Zelazny has a unique quirkiness in his narration that speaks directly to me, and <i>A Night in the Lonesome October</i> which I read in one breath over the wee hours of a late October night is no exception.<br><br>Zelazny is a genius when it comes to telling a story. The trick here is the narration - <b>the wonderful, clever narration that gives you zero exposition but instead throws you into the thick of events to let you sink or swim</b>, and once you decide to swim you get a slow trickle of hints and clues along the way until you reach a point where you no longer remember how exactly you figured out all the goings-on - or rather not all but some, as even after the wrap-up there remain the unexplored paths and corners that make you realize that you just barely scratched the surface under which there are more tantalizing depths. <br><br>All of this is infused with clever, wry, and sometimes dark humor and peppered with smart allusions that feel organic and not, as in the hands of a less skilled writer they could be, pretentious. And eventually a vivid picture full of Zelazny's sophisticated and crisp imagery emerges -<b> a much bigger and fuller picture than anything initially suggested, and it's lovely and menacing and dark and light at the same time.</b> And I love it.<br><br>It's a light and clever tale with Lovecraftian overtones, set in the whereabouts of London in the late Victorian era and featuring a mishmash of the beloved and not-so-beloved characters of that time: Jack (the Ripper), Larry Talbot (The Wolfman), the Great Detective (Sherlock Holmes), the Count (Dracula), the Good Doctor (Frankenstein) and such, all gathered with their familiars for a <b>"Game"</b> played a few times a century when full moon falls on October 31st, a Game which can decide the fate of the world, a Game full of bizarre rituals and<i>"lunatic scavenger hunts", </i>a Game which may or may not open the way into our world to the Elder Gods. In the Game it is a well-kept secret which player is on which side, and the location of the grand showdown needs to be figured out quickly but keeps shifting depending on which players choose to join. <blockquote>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1414344939i/11642546.jpg" width="340" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</blockquote>And sometimes there just may be a hilarious body parts exchange during frantic digging in the cemetery that made me choke with laughter sometime around 3 am:<blockquote>
  <i>“Damn! I need a left femur and this one ain't got one!"<br>"Left femur, you say?" came an ancient croaking voice from nearby, which could have been Owen's. "I've one right here I ain't usin'. Have you a liver, though? That's my need."<br>"Easily done!" came the reply. "Bide a moment. There! Trade?"<br>"You have it! Catch!"<br>Something flashed through the air to rattle farther down the hill, followed by scurrying sounds.<br>"Fair enough! Here's yer liver!"<br>There came a splap from higher up and a muttered "Got it!"<br>"Hey!" came a lady's voice then, from off to the left. "While you're about it, have you a skull?"<br>"Indeed I do!" said the second man. "What'll you give?"<br>"What do you need?"<br>"Fingerbones!"<br>"Done! I'll tie 'em together with a piece of twine!"<br>"Here's your skull!"<br>"Got it! Yours'll be along shortly!"<br>"Has anyone the broken vertebrae of a hanged man?" came a deep masculine voice with a Hungarian accent, from somewhere far to the right.”</i>
</blockquote>And who is better to figure out the plot threads than <b>our narrator, a gifted thaumaturgical calculator, also known as Snuff, Jack Ripper's dog (or perhaps, a tad <u>more</u> than your usual canine)</b>, the spy, the plotter, and the only one to keep in check the menaces of <i>“the Thing in the Circle, the Thing in the Wardrobe, and the Thing in the Steamer Trunk, not to mention the Things in the Mirror.”</i> Snuff, whose keen sense for animal politics and a knack for knowing when to form alliances with the other familiars (Bubo the rat making me laugh!) and when to strategically share information may be the deciding factor in the battle for the fate of this world. Snuff, whom I love dearly even though I'm decidedly not a "dog person".<blockquote>
  <i>"Hi. I'm a watchdog."<br>"Me, too."<br>"I've been watching you."<br>"And I've been watching you."<br>"Why is your person digging a big hole?"<br>"There are some things down there that he needs."<br>"Oh. I don't think he's supposed to be doing that."<br>"May I see your teeth?"<br>"Yes. Here. May I see yours?"<br>"Of course."<br>"Perhaps it's all right. Do you think you might leave a large bone somewhere nearby?"</i>
</blockquote><b>Yes, Roger Zelazny is indeed a genius who clearly had such a great time writing this story that the fun is infectious. </b>Whichever genre this little gem of a book falls in - comedy or Gothic horror or detective mystery - there is no doubt that it's the work of a confident master and a delight to read, especially on a dark and lonesome late October night.<blockquote>
  <i>“I took Jack his slippers this evening and lay at his feet before a roaring fire while he smoked his pipe, sipped sherry, and read the newspaper. He read aloud everything involving killings, arsons, mutilations, grave robberies, church desecrations, and unusual thefts.<b> It is very pleasant just being domestic sometimes</b>.”</i>
</blockquote><br>————<br><br>2020 Halloween re-read: This book will never fail to bring me giddy happiness and joy.<br>“Opener or closer?”</span>
  <a data-text-id="6696659716175626955" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1261310910" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1261310910" />
    <a title="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8734459-tadiana-night-owl"><img alt="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603085284p2/8734459.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1261310910?book_show_action=true">Oct 24, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" href="/user/show/8734459-tadiana-night-owl">Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽ by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/9340136-evgeny">Evgeny</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=vampires-and-werewolves-oh-my">vampires-and-werewolves-oh-my</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=victorian">victorian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=things-go-bump-in-the-night">things-go-bump-in-the-night</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=humor">humor</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1261310910" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4197299129829204479">Review first posted on <a href='http://www.fantasyliterature.com/reviews/a-night-in-the-lonesome-october/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Fantasy Literature</a>:<br/><br/>During the entire month of October, in the late 1800s, in a year when the full moon falls on Halloween, strange forces gather in a village outside of London.<br/><br/> <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1413418724i/11507944.jpg' width='300' height='335' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/>Various iconic characters ― who will be familiar to fans of Victorian literature and classic horror movies ― create shifting alliances, gather herbs, instruments of power and the odd eyeball and femur, and prepare for a mystery-shrouded event that will take place on Halloween night.<br/><br/><i>A Night in the L</i></span>
  <span id="freeText4197299129829204479" style="display:none">Review first posted on <a href="http://www.fantasyliterature.com/reviews/a-night-in-the-lonesome-october/" rel="nofollow noopener">Fantasy Literature</a>:<br><br>During the entire month of October, in the late 1800s, in a year when the full moon falls on Halloween, strange forces gather in a village outside of London.<br><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1413418724i/11507944.jpg" width="300" height="335" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Various iconic characters ― who will be familiar to fans of Victorian literature and classic horror movies ― create shifting alliances, gather herbs, instruments of power and the odd eyeball and femur, and prepare for a mystery-shrouded event that will take place on Halloween night.<br><br><i>A Night in the Lonesome October</i>, published in 1993, is narrated by the aptly-named Snuff, a dog who is the familiar of a man named Jack. Snuff is more than just a dog; at the beginning of the novel he comments cryptically, “I like being a watchdog better than what I was before he summoned me and gave me this job.” Snuff helps Jack gather ingredients for Halloween night, keeps an watchful eye on various cursed Things trapped in Jack’s house, and draws lines between the houses of the various players to create a diagram that will help him and Jack in their planning for … whatever it is that will happen on Halloween.<br><br>Snuff also cautiously communicates with other animals in the neighborhood: Quicklime, a black snake belonging to a mad monk named Rastov; Graymalk the cat, who is the familiar of a witch called Crazy Jill; a rat named Bubo who lives with a man called the “Good Doctor”; Needle, a bat who associates with the Count; and others. Snuff explains that it’s complicated at the beginning of the month because he has no way of knowing whether these people and their familiars are “openers” or “closers.” What openers and closers are remains mysterious until much later in the story, but it’s clear it’s at the root of the great Game they are playing and the ultimate contest to occur between the players on Halloween night. Meanwhile, the Great Detective lurks about the area with his companion, occasionally donning disguises in the course of his investigation (which don’t fool Snuff, of course).<br><br>A Night in the Lonesome October is creepy yet humorous, gruesome and witty at the same time. One of the highlights is a grave-robbing scene in which several players spend an evening gathering ingredients, with various bodily parts flying through the air in a macabre game of catch:<blockquote>“Eyeballs, anyone?” came a call.<br>“Over here,” said someone with a Russian accent. “One of them, please.”<br>“I’ll have the other,” came an aristocratic voice from the opposite direction.<br>“Either of you got a couple of floating ribs, or a pair of kidneys?”<br>“Down here, on the kidneys!” came a new voice. “And I’m in need of a patella!”<br>“What’s that?”<br>“Knee bone!”<br> “Oh? No problem.…”</blockquote>Roger Zelazny cheerfully hides identities and key plot points from his readers during the early part of the Game, allowing us to work out for ourselves who and what they are, whether they’re working for good or evil, and what exactly is going down on Halloween night. The Count and the Great Detective are fairly easy, Jack and the Good Doctor probably won’t take a whole lot longer, and Larry Talbot reveals himself fairly early on (even if you’re not already familiar with his name). But most of the others will take more puzzling out. Fans of <i>A Night in the Lonesome October</i>, which has developed a cult following, devote <a href="https://lovecraftzine.com/magazine/issues/2012-2/issue-18-october-2012/fallen-books-and-other-subtle-clues-in-zelaznys-a-night-in-the-lonesome-october-by-dr-christopher-s-kovacs/" rel="nofollow noopener">entire web pages</a> to analyzing the identities of and inspirations for various minor characters (you should check these pages out only after you’ve finished the book, as they’re riddled with spoilers). It was delightful to read and unpack all the layers of meaning hidden in the text. Any book that reveals more and more layers and depth and connections, as you reread and analyze it, gets a large rating boost from me. I’ll freely admit that it brought back the best of my memories of deep discussions in college English lit courses.<br><br>The characterization is excellent. Minor characters like the Count and the Great Detective shine in their limited but key scenes, surprising us at key turns. Snuff, despite his intelligence and sense of humor, remains clearly a dog in his nature and concerns. His gradually developing alliance and even friendship with the cat Graymalk reminded me of the relationship between my own family’s Siamese mix cat and Labrador retriever. Snuff’s master Jack is intelligent and kind but is also, Snuff explains, “under a curse from long ago and must do much of his work at night to keep worse things from happening.” Jack and Snuff get along very well.<blockquote>I took Jack his slippers this evening and lay at his feet before a roaring fire while he smoked his pipe, sipped sherry, and read the newspaper. He read aloud everything involving killings, arsons, mutilations, grave robberies, church desecrations, and unusual thefts. It is very pleasant just being domestic sometimes.</blockquote>There’s a longstanding rumor (which, as far as I can tell, has never been confirmed) that A Night in the Lonesome October arose out of a bet someone made with Zelazny that he couldn’t write a story where readers would root for Jack the Ripper. I think you would be hard-pressed to find a reader who would claim Zelazny lost that bet.<br><br>There are 31 chapters in <i>A Night in the Lonesome October</i>, one for each day in October. It’s great pulpy fun, but with an underlying intelligence and dry humor. I can see why reading <i>A Night in the Lonesome October</i> has become an annual October ritual for so many fans!<br><br>Thanks to Evgeny and the 2017 AND 2018 buddy reads with the Roger Zelazny Newbie group!</span>
  <a data-text-id="4197299129829204479" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

Now let's dance and stuff.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1604225023ra/30318347.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1479540926i/21203689._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>[<b>October 2019</b>]<br/><br/>➽ <b>

  <span id="freeText15463649609672998863" style="display:none">➽ <b>
  <u>And the moral of this rerereread is</u>
</b>: there ain't nothing like the <b>Grand Graveyard Decaying Body Part Swap Thingie</b> (GGDBPST™), if you ask me. Now let's dance and stuff.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1604225023ra/30318347.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1479540926i/21203689._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>[<b>October 2019</b>]<br><br>➽ <b>
  <u>And the moral of this rereread is</u>
</b>: pack rats named after the bubonic plague <b>underestimate thou shalt not</b>. <br><br>➽ <b>
  <u>And the <i>other</i> moral of this rereread is</u>
</b>: pack rats named after the bubonic plague and that are <b>friends</b> with dogs that are <b>friends</b> with cats <b>Super Extra Especially Wary Of</b> (SE²WO™) thou shalt be and stuff.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1572598707i/28385344.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>P.S.</b> Jack and Jill did NOT go up the hill. I repeat, Jack and Jill did NOT go up the hill. Just so you know. <b>You are quite welcome</b>.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1479540926i/21203689._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>[<b>October 2018</b>]<br><br>🎃 <b>Impromptu and Not So Lonesome October Buddy Reread</b> (IaNSLBR™) with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1261310910" rel="nofollow noopener">Tadiana</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/756506537" rel="nofollow noopener">Evgeny</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2549608517" rel="nofollow noopener">OhWell</a> 🎃<br><br><b><u>Original rating</u>: 3 stars</b>. <br><b><u>New rating</u>: 5 stars</b>. <i>Does that mean there might be hope for me yet? Oh dear. We are all doomed, methinks.</i><br><br>➽ <b>
  <u>And the moral of this reread is</u>
</b>: hallelujah to our Lord Shrimp and stuff! I finally saw the light! And <b>read the book right</b>! (Yes, I know, it rhymes. Yes, I know, I’m a poet.) <s>The Evil Russians™</s> Someone should give me a <b>lifetime achievement award</b> or something. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1572598611i/28385321.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>Okay, well, yeah, that’s very nice and stuff, but I was thinking more along the lines of a, um, you know, liquid, amber-colored “<a href="https://www.adweek.com/files/imagecache/node-blog/laphroaig-opinions-2014_4.jpg" rel="nofollow noopener">or something</a>” from Scotland, you know.</i><br><br>➽ <b>
  <u>And the <i>other</i> moral of this reread is</u>
</b>: I’m doing the <b>Poof Gone Harem</b>™ on <b>Snuff</b>, and he will be joining the rest of the <s>scary, creepy as fish</s> fluffy, cuddly <s>creatures</s> mongrels in my <b>Most Wondrous If Slightly Freakish High Security Petting Zoo</b> (MWISFHSPZ™) pronto. So yay and stuff.<br><br>➽ <b>
  <u>And the <i>other, other</i> moral of this reread is</u>
</b>: this book features the mostest bestest and wittiest <s>animal</s> familiar dialogues in the history of <b>Mostest Bestest and Wittiest <s>Animal</s> Familiar Dialogues</b> (MBaW<s>A</s>FD™). And that is a <b>scientifically proven fact</b>.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1541090150ra/26533349.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>See, even Gertrude agrees with me on that one. And Gertrude knows loads about scientifically proven facts. LOADS.</i> <br><br><b>P.S.</b> I do stand by what I said the first time around: <b>body part transactions FTW</b>!<br><b>P.P.S.</b> Only <b>334 days to go</b> until we ritually rereread this book and stuff. The countdown has begun and stuff. Not that I look forward to it and stuff. Just stating a fact and stuff. <b>Obviously and stuff</b>.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1479540926i/21203689._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>[<b>October 2017</b>]<br><br>• <b>Everyone Luuuuurved It But Me Now that's a Surprise Buddy Read</b> (ELIBMNtaSBR™) with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/756506537" rel="nofollow noopener">Evgeny</a> (aka The Culprit), <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1261310910" rel="nofollow noopener">Tadiana</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2165177725" rel="nofollow noopener">Choko</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1606278722" rel="nofollow noopener">Layla</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1941540500" rel="nofollow noopener">Maria</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2162155997" rel="nofollow noopener">Robin</a> •<br><br><b>So this was me</b> while I was reading this book:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1538471921ra/26387751.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><s>Shrimpless</s> <b>Needless to say</b>, I wasn't in the best of dispositions to read this <b>classic Halloween read</b>. By the way, worry not for I am not going to explain again how <b>slightly pointless</b> the whole Halloween read thing is to me, because <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1428989954" rel="nofollow noopener">been there done that</a> and all that crap. Anyway, Halloween + <b>Evgeny's disastrous influence on my reading life</b> = here we are. <br><br><b>First off</b>, I should mention that <s>I've had too much whisky</s> I usually have a <b>very low tolerance for animals in books</b> <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  <i>except for IA beasts and creatures. But, as we all know, IA doesn't count. Because, whatever it is, IA does it better</i>
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. So imagine my cry of utter delight when I realized this story was told <b>from a charming dog's POV</b>. I mean, I was totally, like, YAY and stuff <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[← <i>this might or might not be a slightly ironic statement</i> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. BUT. I must admit that Snuff, the dog in question, is <b>pretty cool</b>. He happens to be Jack the <s>Stripper</s> Ripper's dog, which worked a lot in his favor, <b>for obvious homicidal reasons</b>. You would think that good old Jack would have picked a <b>more badass name</b> for his dog, by the way. Llike, I don't know, Cleaver or Butcher or Cutter or something. But I guess you can't have everything. Anyway, the dog is pretty <b>smart and witty and bearable</b> for a pathetic animal, so I survived reading from his POV. Not only that, I also managed to make it <b>relatively unscarred</b> to the very last page, despite half of the cast being <b>bloody shrimping fauna material</b>! Nothing short of a miracle, if you ask me. <b>Allellujah to our Lord Shrimp and stuff</b>.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1509389309ra/24315745.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>So yes</b>, as much as I am loathe to admit, the animals in this story are <b>pretty cool</b>. They are actually <b>more interesting</b> than the, um, human characters in the story. Which is a shame considering the cast consists not only of our chum <b>Jack</b>, but also of Count <s>Premolar</s> <b>Dracula</b>, Dr <s>It's Alive</s> <b>Frankenstein</b> (and his baby, of course), <b>Rasputin</b> of the Super Hot Sexy Beard, <s>Benedryl Cabbagepatch</s> <s>Benedict Cumberbatch</s> <b>Sherlock</b> Himself, a guy called <b>Spoiler Spoiler Spoiler</b> (not his real name) and a whole bunch of other people. A whole bunch of <b>very male people</b>, I might add, and <b>only one bloody shrimping woman</b>. Which is slightly <b>not cool</b>, Mr Zelazny. The shrimps are not pleased. And neither am I <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  <br>
  <br>
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1506765718ra/24050477.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  <br>
  <br>
  <i>I'm pretty hot in that outfit, I know.</i>
  <br>
  <br>
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. Anyway, with such an <b>awesome clique of awesome characters,</b> you'd think the book would be, you know, awesome and stuff, right? Right. Ha. <b>Wrong</b>. I mean, it's definitely not bad, and the writing is really <b>good and humorous and witty and clever and stuff</b> but the whole thing felt kind of *looks around to make sure Evgeny isn't on the premises* *whispers* <b>meh</b>. I guess I was expecting something <b>darker and scarier and creepier and horrifyinger</b> (yes, that is a word) and this just felt terribly *checks behind her back in case Evgeny is trying to cunningly sneak up on her* *whispers* <b>light and decaf and sugar-free and stuff</b>.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1509390432ra/24315819.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>Yes, that's pretty much how spooky this book was. Ew ew ew.</i> <br><br><b>Some barnacles</b> might say that I didn't fully appreciate the book because it takes <s>bloody ages</s> half of the story for <s>under-performing shrimps like me</s> the reader to understand <b>what the fish is going on</b>. Wrong wrong wrong. <b>The King of Totally Confusing Befuddlement</b> (KoTCB™), aka Glen Cook, is my master and, let me tell you, I have come out unscathed of much more <b>perplexingly confounding</b> tales than this one. It's the lack of confusion I usually find confusion. <b>So QED and stuff</b>. <br><br><b>Anything else?</b> Apart from the fact that I obviously read this book wrong, you mean? Nah, don't think so. <br><br>» And the moral of this <b><s>Eagerly</s> Apprehensively Waiting for Evgeny's Revenge Now That I've Gone and Done the Unthinking Unforgivable and Rated this Much Beloved Book of His Three Pathetic Little Stars Crappy Non Review</b> (<s>E</s>AWfERNtIGaDtUUaRtMBBoHTPLSCNR™) is: I am not worthy. <b>Obviously</b>. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1509391629ra/24315914.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>P.S.</b> Body parts transactions FTW!<br><b>P.P.S.</b> What kind of botched-up ending is this, Mr Zelazny? Just asking for a friend.<br><b>P.P.P.S.S.S.</b> Gahan Wilson's illustrations for this book are slightly awesome. And you are slightly welcome.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1479540926i/21203689._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>[ <b>Pre-review nonsense</b>]<br><br><s><b><u>Actual rating</u>: 3.5 stars</b>.</s><br><br><b>Subcontracting</b> this crappy non-review to Graymalk the cat. She's hard at work right now, and should be able to deliver a <b>most entertaining reading report</b> post haste. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1572599398ra/28385389.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>➽ Full <b>Please Forgive Me Evgeny For I Have Sinned and Failed to Give this Decidedly Not Spooky Tale a 5 Star Rating Blame the Tourist Hordes of Doom Don't Blame Me Crappy Non Review</b> (PFMEFIHSaFtGtDNTTa5SRBtTHoDDBMCNR™) to come.</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/964883514?book_show_action=true">Jun 11, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Delee" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Delee" href="/user/show/6168268-delee">Delee</a>

        rated it

<span id="freeTextContainer1957995486365530688">Soooooooooooooooooo this was a group read I forced upon my nearest and dearest- I looooove my GR gals- even if you hated or loved every minute of it ladieeeeeees!!<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1413418724i/11507944.jpg' alt=' photo 34363027-cdce-41e6-a820-9a7418c90cc9_zps9ffd7431.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><i>I am a watchdog. My name is Snuff. I live with my master Jack outside of London now. I like Soho very much at night with its smelly fogs and dark streets. It is silent then and we go for long walks....</i><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1413418724i/11507945.jpg' alt=' photo d0bcdcef-060b-4458-84b6-338a085beb4a_zpsa708a9f4.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>The story of A NIGHT IN LONESOME OCTOBER is told in a prologue and thirty-one chapters- one for each day in October. I read it in three.</span>
  <span id="freeText1957995486365530688" style="display:none">Soooooooooooooooooo this was a group read I forced upon my nearest and dearest- I looooove my GR gals- even if you hated or loved every minute of it ladieeeeeees!!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1413418724i/11507944.jpg" alt=" photo 34363027-cdce-41e6-a820-9a7418c90cc9_zps9ffd7431.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>I am a watchdog. My name is Snuff. I live with my master Jack outside of London now. I like Soho very much at night with its smelly fogs and dark streets. It is silent then and we go for long walks....</i><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1413418724i/11507945.jpg" alt=" photo d0bcdcef-060b-4458-84b6-338a085beb4a_zpsa708a9f4.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The story of A NIGHT IN LONESOME OCTOBER is told in a prologue and thirty-one chapters- one for each day in October. I read it in three...sometimes you just can't wait...<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1413418724i/11507946.jpg" alt=" photo 833b75df-d5c1-4bba-8ea8-fc04c29fa0d8_zpseab57893.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Every once in a while- when the moon is full on a Halloween night- a group gathers and a game begins...The game of saving the world from evil and destruction- who is on the right side and who is on the wrong one??? I guess you will have to read it to find out...<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1413418724i/11507947.jpg" alt=" photo 56fd114e-19fe-40ea-afef-442c9de8a1a1_zps7372d5d5.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>"Hi. I'm a watchdog."<br>"Me, too."<br>"I've been watching you."<br>"And I've been watching you."<br>"Why is your person digging a big hole?"<br>"There are some things down there that he needs."<br>"Oh, I don't think he's supposed to be doing that."<br>"May I see your teeth?"<br>"Yes. Here. May I see yours?"<br>"Of course." </i><br><br>October-1887- a small English village finds itself host to a strange group of visitors. They are players in "The Game", and on the final night- they will declare their allegiances in a contest that will determine the future of the world. Until then- there are mystic artifacts to track down, rituals to complete and allies to make...but appearances can be deceiving- and who they might think of as friends...could be their enemies.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1413418724i/11507948.jpg" alt=" photo 0c2e738a-9734-4535-8a0e-0a82a00d56dc_zpsf9b46c07.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>If I can recommend only one book to read in October- this would be it! It may not be for everyone...but it certainly was for me. So much fuuuuuuuuuun!!!<br><br>Happy (almost) Halloween!!</span>

<div id="review_1881309810" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1881309810" />
    <a title="Vishnu Chevli" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/47278120-vishnu-chevli"><img alt="Vishnu Chevli" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1539487526p2/47278120.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1881309810?book_show_action=true">Feb 25, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Vishnu Chevli" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Vishnu Chevli" href="/user/show/47278120-vishnu-chevli">Vishnu Chevli</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/32322092-a-night-in-the-lonesome-october">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47278120-vishnu-chevli?shelf=ebooks">ebooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47278120-vishnu-chevli?shelf=english">english</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1881309810" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14577146489998151557"><b>Imagine a brave Scooby-Doo at Work</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1488107265i/22081112._SX540_.png' width='400' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I rarely get chance to read a highly admired book. "A Night in the Lonesome October" by Roger Zelazny is my first review read from Netgalley. Whether you call the genre humour or horror or lovecraftian or mystery, but I am not able to put it into single genre confidently. Unlike my other review reads this book shows clear cut difference between debut author and veteran author.<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1488107157i/22081098._SX540_.jpg' width='400' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I think one has to read the book to understand what the story is all about. And many re</span>
  <span id="freeText14577146489998151557" style="display:none"><b>Imagine a brave Scooby-Doo at Work</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1488107265i/22081112._SX540_.png" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I rarely get chance to read a highly admired book. "A Night in the Lonesome October" by Roger Zelazny is my first review read from Netgalley. Whether you call the genre humour or horror or lovecraftian or mystery, but I am not able to put it into single genre confidently. Unlike my other review reads this book shows clear cut difference between debut author and veteran author.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1488107157i/22081098._SX540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I think one has to read the book to understand what the story is all about. And many reviewers mentioned that it takes half the novel read to get the idea of the story. I would like to correct it, it took me more than two third of the book to understand what is happening. Story is written from watchdog's point of view. In a certain area of London, during Halloween of 1880's, a group of people (with special powers) gathered to perform a particular ceremony. They call it the Game. Each player has their own companion (animals) who help them during the Game. Players are divided into two groups, the Openers and the Closers. This year's Game became dangerous because of the death of players from both the sides. Snuff, watchdog, and Gray, cat, venture their own adventures during Game to find out truth behind various strange events. You will find all type of characters in story, a magician, a witch, a vampire, a warewolf, a psychopath, a Frankenstein and many more.<br><br>There were some illustration given at appropriate places to clear readers doubt. For an example, from an illustration I understood that one player was a vampire, otherwise I would have kept thinking how a person sleeps in coffin under debris. You need a good amount of patience to finish this book. For some it may be nail biting journey and for some it may be sure shot DNFs. Its good that I sustained first 100 pages otherwise I would have put it under DNFs.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14577146489998151557" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2165177725" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2165177725" />
    <a title="Choko" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/27962805-choko"><img alt="Choko" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1475642755p2/27962805.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2165177725?book_show_action=true">Oct 26, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Choko" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Choko" href="/user/show/27962805-choko">Choko</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27962805-choko?shelf=demons">demons</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27962805-choko?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27962805-choko?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27962805-choko?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/27962805-choko?shelf=humor">humor</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2165177725" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6623365929669193967"><b>*** 5 +++ ***<br/><br/>A buddy read with the Roger Zelazny Newbies Group, since we wanted to start with a bang!!!</b><br/><br/>Where do I start??? Let's begin with my thanks to Evgeny, who had the good sense to invite several of us for the Halloween Read and made us read it! Thank you!!! <br/><br/>I had no idea what I was getting myself into. After all, I am not a horror reading type of a gal. However, I believe Horror is the last thing I would associate <i>A Night in Lonesome October</i> with. The first would be smart and second, funn</span>
  <span id="freeText6623365929669193967" style="display:none"><b>*** 5 +++ ***<br /><br />A buddy read with the Roger Zelazny Newbies Group, since we wanted to start with a bang!!!</b><br /><br />Where do I start??? Let's begin with my thanks to Evgeny, who had the good sense to invite several of us for the Halloween Read and made us read it! Thank you!!! <br /><br />I had no idea what I was getting myself into. After all, I am not a horror reading type of a gal. However, I believe Horror is the last thing I would associate <i>A Night in Lonesome October</i> with. The first would be smart and second, funny. It is like a Halloween Scavenger Hunt of Classic Characters, all of them counting the days from the First of October to The Night, the Thirty First. <br /><br /><b>
  <i>"..."I am a watchdog. My name is Snuff.... I fetch things for Jack on occasion—his wand, his big knife with the old writing on the sides. I always know just when he needs them because it is my job to watch and to know. I like being a watchdog better than what I was before he summoned me and gave me this job...."..."</i>
</b><br /><br />We are told the story, happening in Victorian London, from the POV of Snuff, the watch dog familiar to Jack of dubious fame from that time period. As I said, the book is loaded with clues and connections, which are a delight to decipher, and I have to say, doing it in a group is much more fun, because if you missed something, your buddy reader might have figured it out and it truly feels like a game! You start from no knowledge at all, and then you get pieces little by little, with every chapter covering a day in October and giving us some more players and clues to go with. It becomes obvious pretty quickly that teams of "openers" or "closers" are being created, but no one knows who is on which team... <br /><br /><b>
  <i>"..."I addressed the squirrel through a hedge:<br />“Are you in the Game?”<br />It scurried to the man’s nearer shoulder and peered.<br />“Who asks?” it chattered.<br />“Call me Snuff,” I answered.<br />“Call me Cheeter,” it replied. “Yes, I suppose we are. Last minute thing—rush, rush.”<br />“Opener or closer?”<br />“Impolite! Impolite to ask! You know that!”<br />“Just thought I’d try. You could be novices.”<br />“Not new enough to be giving anything away. Leave it at that.”<br />“I will.”<br />“Stay. Is there a black snake in it?”<br />“You ask me to give something away. But yes, there is: Quicklime. Beware. His master is mad.”<br />“Aren’t they all?”<br />We chuckled and I faded away."..."</i>
</b><br /><br />Needless to say, the familiars were the main characters, since we saw everything from the point of view of a dog. This is what made the story even more enchanting than it already would have been, given the brilliant way the author lets us in on it. Snuff is not only a great watch dog and assistant to Jack, he is also a mathematical genius who sees and deciphers patterns and even knows when to act like a lovable goof of a dog too!!! I am in love with this character and if Jack and Jill don't work out, I can take on the care for Snuff and Graymalk the cat at any time - voluntarily, this is how willing I am to work for the greater good!!! <br /><br /><b>
  <i>"..."“The crazy witch’s companion may be running out of steam about now.”<br />“What do you mean?”<br />“‘Ding, dong, dell.’”<br />“I don’t follow you.”<br />“Literally. Pussy’s in the well.”<br />“Who threw her in?”<br />“MacCab, full of sin.”<br />“Where is it?”<br />“By the outhouse, full of shit. Back of Crazy Jill’s place. Keeps it from going dry, I guess.”"..."</i>
</b><br /><br />The banter is almost as awesome as the structure and simplicity of the storytelling. I think half of the book is quotable, but to truly experience it, I would recommend you to get several friends together and read it, preferably some time in October:):):) You will enjoy the way the characters gather their needed materials, which are supposed to be acquired in some very specific ways and times... Zelazny exhibits a particular talent in knowing when less is more and makes our imaginations work overtime with the hints he gives here and there. I am not sure I can find a weakness in the whole thing at all, and I am not even going to look for it. I just enjoyed it and the way it made me always look for the second meaning of every word and hint, making my brain feel full of champagne bubbles and kept me slightly buzzed throughout! Evgeny, you recruited me into the Legions of RZ's fans! Thank you once again! <br /><br /><b>
  <i>"..."“I took Jack his slippers this evening and lay at his feet before a roaring fire while he smoked his pipe, sipped sherry, and read the newspaper. He read aloud everything involving killings, arsons, mutilations, grave robberies, church desecrations, and unusual thefts. It is very pleasant just being domestic sometimes.” "..."</i>
</b><br /><br />Now I wish you all Happy Reading and many more wonderful books to come!!! </span>
  <a data-text-id="6623365929669193967" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/870755-dan-schwent?shelf=pants-shittingly-awesome">pants-shittingly-awesome</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/870755-dan-schwent?shelf=zelazny">zelazny</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/870755-dan-schwent?shelf=plan-on-rereading-one-day">plan-on-rereading-one-day</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/870755-dan-schwent?shelf=great-titles">great-titles</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer48090222" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10864754871556448026">A Night in the Lonesome October is about a gateway to a dimension of Lovecraftian horrors and the two opposing forces dedicated to opening the gate or making sure it stays closed. The story is told from the point of view of Jack the Ripper's dog Snuff. Yeah, you read that right.<br/><br/>I was hooked right away, around the time Snuff and the graveyard dog had a funny conversation and asked to see one another's teeth. One of the characters calls The Game, as it is known, a lunatic scavenger hunt. That's pr</span>
  <span id="freeText10864754871556448026" style="display:none">A Night in the Lonesome October is about a gateway to a dimension of Lovecraftian horrors and the two opposing forces dedicated to opening the gate or making sure it stays closed. The story is told from the point of view of Jack the Ripper's dog Snuff. Yeah, you read that right.<br /><br />I was hooked right away, around the time Snuff and the graveyard dog had a funny conversation and asked to see one another's teeth. One of the characters calls The Game, as it is known, a lunatic scavenger hunt. That's pretty much what it is. Snuff spends most of the book calculating where the gateway will appear, having to recalculate every time a player turns up dead...<br /><br />One of the best parts of A Night in the Lonsesome October is trying to figure out which characters are actually participants in The Game, and which side they are on.<br /><br />I enjoyed seeing classic horror characters like Count Dracula, Larry Talbot, and Frankenstein's monster in the same story as Sherlock Holmes and Jack the Ripper. Through in the Cthulhu mythos and you have a ripping good yarn.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10864754871556448026" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
