<div id="review_10673657" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/10673657" />
    <a title="Jim" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/695116-jim"><img alt="Jim" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1340192527p2/695116.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/10673657?book_show_action=true">Dec 19, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jim" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jim" href="/user/show/695116-jim">Jim</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/695116-jim?shelf=horror">horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/695116-jim?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/695116-jim?shelf=1paper">1paper</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/695116-jim?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/695116-jim?shelf=2fiction">2fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer10673657" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer242443696191763499">An entertaining, interesting story on the face, the understory is even better. Zelazny's sheer number of allusions and amount of sources truly make it a lunatic scavenger hunt that lead to research in some very dark & dusty corners of history, film, myth, & writing.<br/><br/>2019: Read with SciFi and Fantasy Book Club, invited by Anna.<br/><a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://www.goodreads.com/topic/show/20564459'>https://www.goodreads.com/topic/show/...</a><br/><br/>2017: Read with ? group?<br/><br/>2012: Re-reading yet again with the Beyond Reality group.<br/>By Day: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://www.goodreads.com/topic/show/1045627'>http://www.goodreads.com/topic/show/1...</a><br/>Cove</span>
  <span id="freeText242443696191763499" style="display:none">An entertaining, interesting story on the face, the understory is even better. Zelazny's sheer number of allusions and amount of sources truly make it a lunatic scavenger hunt that lead to research in some very dark &amp; dusty corners of history, film, myth, &amp; writing.<br /><br />2019: Read with SciFi and Fantasy Book Club, invited by Anna.<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/topic/show/20564459">https://www.goodreads.com/topic/show/...</a><br /><br />2017: Read with ? group?<br /><br />2012: Re-reading yet again with the Beyond Reality group.<br />By Day: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/topic/show/1045627">http://www.goodreads.com/topic/show/1...</a><br />Cover &amp; other Art: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/topic/show/1045641">http://www.goodreads.com/topic/show/1...</a><br />Both of these topics contain spoilers. <br /><br />I'm armed with 20 pages of notes &amp; a copy of the cover art. We're having a great discussion with some additional pieces being filled in. This is definitely a book best enjoyed with a mixed group. Those who haven't read it before bring new ways of looking at the mystery as it unfolds &amp; that suggests new avenues of research. All our diverse experience still leaves a few lingering mysteries.<br /><br />I posted the cover photo with numbers on it for each character &amp; we're trying to figure out who is who. Many are easy, but a few are about impossible. I contacted James Warhola again, but he still doesn't have access to his notes. Maybe next year. Yes, I'll likely read it again that soon, so I had to give it 5 stars. It's a gift that never stops giving. <br /><br />It was a great discussion &amp; I added some new information to my notes. <br /><br />---------------<br />2010 &amp; 2011: Read in the Zelazny group. Spoiler topic here:<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/topic/show/218652">http://www.goodreads.com/topic/show/2...</a><br />About 150 posts as we dissected the book to find all the allusions &amp; sources Zelazny drew from. Wow!<br /><br />I wrote up notes &amp; contacted the cover artist Warhola.<br /><br />----------- <br />2008: Re-reading for the SF/Fantasy monthly &amp; loved it. It's a fast, fun read &amp; has the quality I've come to expect from Zelazny. The story, as one of the character's of the book puts it, is 'a lunatic scavenger hunt' in more ways than one. Who are the people, what are they trying to accomplish - are they good or bad guys? It's also perfect Halloween reading.<br /><br />There are 31 chapters, one for each day of the month of October during which the story plays out. The early chapters are short, but they grow longer as our understanding of the story progresses - the plot thickens &amp; so do the details. <br /><br />At first, we're not quite sure what is happening, but the characters are interesting. The story is filled with unlikely heroes &amp; villains who make unlikely alliances &amp; friendships. The characters, their names &amp; other references were fun reading up on. Many are pulled from all over classic horror &amp; the real world. Some I knew, others I vaguely recognized &amp; some I'm still not too certain of. As usual, his novels are worthy of a re-read at a later date.<br /><br />The copy I have is illustrated in B&amp;W. I didn't care much for them &amp; found them more of a distraction than anything. Usually, I ignored them.</span>
  <a data-text-id="242443696191763499" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

      <a href="/user/show/9340136-evgeny">Evgeny</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43587353-orient?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1788917582" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10076771235753117096"><b>Evgeny</b>, thanks again for a great recommendation :)<br/><br/>This book is a great blend of mystery spices, gripping suspense, funny dialogues and fabulous fantasy. Mr. Zelazny’s writing style just enchanted me: so straightforward, smooth and so compelling at the same time, with no difficult words or complex descriptions. The story simply is a page-turner.<br/><br/>What gripped me in A Night in the Lonesome October? Definitely the talking animals, the monsters (who entertained Snuff with their mad requests and danger</span>
  <span id="freeText10076771235753117096" style="display:none"><b>Evgeny</b>, thanks again for a great recommendation :)<br><br>This book is a great blend of mystery spices, gripping suspense, funny dialogues and fabulous fantasy. Mr. Zelazny’s writing style just enchanted me: so straightforward, smooth and so compelling at the same time, with no difficult words or complex descriptions. The story simply is a page-turner.<br><br>What gripped me in A Night in the Lonesome October? Definitely the talking animals, the monsters (who entertained Snuff with their mad requests and dangerous plans) and the heroes from other famous and classical books. The author borrowed some characters from fabulous classics (Mary Shelley, Sir Arthur Conan Doyle, Bram Stoker) to create his book as an interesting game. I had so much fun guessing who’s who. <br><br>The book presented the story of a strange Game, a shrewd and sometimes dangerous fight between two groups of players. When the right time comes, they prepare for one special Night in the Lonesome October when the fate of the world is to be decided. I liked the players and their companions. And the most interesting parts to play, went to the awesome talking companions &lt;3<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1413837583i/11570125._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>London had invited a really special group to play the Game. A dangerous gentleman who wanders the streets at night with a knife ( <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[some ties to the Great Ripper? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> ), with his BBF and scheming partner Snuff, a witch in a disguise as a crazy hag, with her comrade sly Graymalk. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1478165809i/21041024._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Snuff managed all the funny dialogues and I really enjoyed his interaction with others.<br><br><i>I moved in a big circle about the hilltop, pissing on stone after stone as I calculated, partly to keep track of the lines, partly in frustration.</i><br><br>A new form of counting :D well now I know why does my dog have to pee on every bush while going for a walk. :D<br> <br><i>"A chihuahua?" The thing in the circle suggested. "Just for laughs?"<br> "Nope," I answered. "Language barrier.”</i><br><br><i>”Remember what they say about cornered rats," he said. "We can be nasty." <br>"I'm sure," I replied. "But what'd be the point? No one wants to hurt you." <br>"You were chasing me."<br> "I wanted to talk to you."<br> "So you brought along a cat."<br> "I can let you talk to her if you don't want to talk to me." I started to withdraw. <br>"No! Wait! I'd rather talk to you!”</i><br><br>Not enough interesting characters? Ok, here lurk some other interesting personalities: an alluring, very RIP noble and his night companion Needle, an old witcher and his nutty partner Cheeter; the mad Russian monk ( <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[some ties to Grigori Rasputin? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> ) with his sneaky hissing BFF Quicklime, a crazy pair of partners, with a whooping comrade Nightwind. Then there is a crazy bloodlusty man of god, with a peculiar companion Tekela. Other colorful personalities: a good doctor with a kindhearted giant and a sneaky Bubo, a furry botanic ( I found him a little bit primitive) and a Great Detective, a master of disguise. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1478165809i/21041025._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The Game is presented quite masterfully, with lots of bits that the reader has to put together to see the whole puzzle. This story is told from Snuff’s POV. I tracked Snuff and the other players in the Game with interested as the story revealed the closeness of great friendships, the great alliances and the nasty treason. The finale revealed some secrets and it was great to have one of the players, I liked, back.<br><br>I have only one complaint. Some characters were not fully developed, I would have liked to know more about their past, their stronger sides and weaknesses. This is the last book that Mr. Zelazny finished ( moreover it was nominated for the Nebula in 1994) and it’s sad that there won’t be any sequel to this book. <br><br><i>Jack and Jill went down the hill. Gray and I ran after.</i><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1478165809i/21041026._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="10076771235753117096" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2162155997" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2486515654478912645">I used to watch How I Met Your Mother and loved all the various challenges that Barney took on because someone in the group said there was no way he could do it. Like picking up girls in overalls or licking the Liberty Bell. <b>So in my head this is how Roger Zelazny responded when someone told him it would be impossible to make Jack the Ripper into a good guy.</b><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1484823012ra/21756683.gif' width='400' height='292' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I always try to read something for the Halloween season. Horror isn’t exactly my genre so I attempt to pick something more mysterious than s</span>
  <span id="freeText2486515654478912645" style="display:none">I used to watch How I Met Your Mother and loved all the various challenges that Barney took on because someone in the group said there was no way he could do it. Like picking up girls in overalls or licking the Liberty Bell. <b>So in my head this is how Roger Zelazny responded when someone told him it would be impossible to make Jack the Ripper into a good guy.</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1484823012ra/21756683.gif" width="400" height="292" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I always try to read something for the Halloween season. Horror isn’t exactly my genre so I attempt to pick something more mysterious than scary and this fit that bill to a T. <br><br>There are a few things that are done really well in this story. First the narrator is a dog, but not just any dog but one with some sort of ties to the supernatural and he is companion to none other than Jack <i>the Ripper</i> but that is never clearly stated. Still it gives a different and unique perspective on his activities.<br><br>The Second is that all the players in the story are from those old horror movies I watched as a kid including Dr. Frankenstein, Rasputin, Dr. Jekyll and Mr. Hyde, Sherlock Holmes, the original Wolf Man, Count Dracula and more. Each one has their own pet familiar AND is working for a big event on Halloween to either release a great power or keep it where it is. Until very close to the end it is hard to say who is on which side.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1509372205i/24313648._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="162" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The Third thing I enjoyed about this set up is that nothing is told to you. Everything is shown and the story teases out a little at a time with hints here and there but nothing overt. Which leads to some pretty big surprises at the end and a twist I really didn’t see coming.<br><br>Overall Mr. Zelazny sold it to me that Jack wasn’t necessarily a bad guy. And I admittedly ended up reading some of the lore on a few of the other characters in the book which added to the Halloween fun of it.<br><br>The main reason that this didn’t get a full 5 stars is the very abrupt end. I thought there would be an epilogue of sorts and there isn’t. I really wanted to know what happened to a few of the other characters but it is left to my own imagination. <br><br>Still if Horror really isn’t your thing and you want something somewhat funny and mysterious then this could definitely add to your enjoyment of October.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2486515654478912645" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer17826581603938265385">There are so many great reviews of this book and I just sat and read my way through most of them. I cannot compete so I will just say thankyou to the SciFi and Fantasy Book Club for introducing me to this author and for organising a wonderful way of reading the book - one chapter a day through the month of October (the book is arranged that way) culminating with the climax on Halloween. <br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/62005.A_Night_in_the_Lonesome_October' title='A Night in the Lonesome October by Roger Zelazny' rel='nofollow noopener'>A Night in the Lonesome October</a> is a fun book, full of famous characters such as Jack the Ripper, Sherlock Hol</span>
  <span id="freeText17826581603938265385" style="display:none">There are so many great reviews of this book and I just sat and read my way through most of them. I cannot compete so I will just say thankyou to the SciFi and Fantasy Book Club for introducing me to this author and for organising a wonderful way of reading the book - one chapter a day through the month of October (the book is arranged that way) culminating with the climax on Halloween. <br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/62005.A_Night_in_the_Lonesome_October" title="A Night in the Lonesome October by Roger Zelazny" rel="nofollow noopener">A Night in the Lonesome October</a> is a fun book, full of famous characters such as Jack the Ripper, Sherlock Holmes and Dracula. The narrator is a dog which sounds silly but is definitely not. There are references and puns aplenty especially as two of the main characters are called Jack and Jill. There is horror as well - digging up body parts in the cemetery, scary moments when our favourite characters nearly meet their ends and much more.<br /><br />This is a book where the author had fun and it is best read slowly and with commentary from other readers. I would have missed so much without that feedback. Pretty sure I will be opening it again on October 1st 2021.</span>

<div id="review_1070813546" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1070813546" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10412493762247541426">How many times have I read Roger Zelazny’s <i>A Night in the Lonesome October</i>? I literally can’t remember if it’s four or five or six. And it never loses its freshness or excitement.<br/><br/>And how do I write a review for this book that will do it justice? So cleverly written, and readers will delight in figuring out one by one who each of the “players” in the game are — many of which are characters from Victorian literature. Even though this was my fourth or more go-round with these characters, I stayed u</span>
  <span id="freeText10412493762247541426" style="display:none">How many times have I read Roger Zelazny’s <i>A Night in the Lonesome October</i>? I literally can’t remember if it’s four or five or six. And it never loses its freshness or excitement.<br /><br />And how do I write a review for this book that will do it justice? So cleverly written, and readers will delight in figuring out one by one who each of the “players” in the game are — many of which are characters from Victorian literature. Even though this was my fourth or more go-round with these characters, I stayed up late to experience the novel’s unique ending all over again. It’s one of the best books I’ve ever read — not just one of the best fantasy or science-fiction books. Want proof? My three children, then teenagers, listened to it <i>twice</i> on car trips, lapping up every word, eager to hear what was to come next. Now that’s magic!<br /><br />Set in Victorian London and the surrounding countryside, <i>A Night in the Lonesome October</i> begins: “I’m a watchdog. My name is Snuff.” But Snuff is no ordinary watchdog — nor is his master any ordinary Jack. Nor are any of their neighbors ordinary. Soon enough you realize who Jack is, and who the Great Detective and his rotund companion, the Count, the Good Doctor, and the other “players” are in a deadly serious game that could well usher in the end of the world as we currently experience it, a game that takes place every time a full moon occurs on that night in the lonesome October, October 31. Although a full moon coincides with Halloween only three or four times in a century, Snuff has played the game many times before. Before the game comes to its thrilling culmination on Halloween night, several players will die, several animal companions will flee, and much blood and mayhem will flow. Significantly, the word <i>Halloween</i>, an abbreviated version of the Christian expression <i>All Hallows’ Eve</i>, is used but once or twice in the book, which details very un-Christian goings-ons. (To reveal any more would ruin the book.) But the book isn’t as dark as it sounds. With lots of irony and wit, <i>A Night in the Lonesome October</i> will make you rue that Zelazny died before penning a sequel. You will recognize the deft allusions to famous characters in fiction, which provides part of the fun in this masterful fantasy novel. <br /><br />If you have the privilege of enjoying the audio version of <i>A Night in the Lonesome October</i>, you will hear Roger Zelazny himself reading it, and he does a magnificent job — before than the average professional reader. You can buy the audio version through <a href="http://speakingvolumes.mybigcommerce.com/a-night-in-the-lonesome-october-by-roger-zelazny-mp3-audiobook-download/" rel="nofollow noopener">Speaking Volumes</a>. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10412493762247541426" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <span id="freeText17872931294433166294" style="display:none">Oh what a fast, fun adventure for us lovers of mystery, fantasy and horror......Narrated by Jack the Ripper's faithful <i>(door opening)</i> guard dog Snuff <i>(with his best pal Graymalk the cat by his side)</i> Roger Zelazny dedicates his <b>last</b> book to some of the GREATS.....Shelley, Poe, Stoker, Doyle, Lovecraft, Bradbury, Bloch, Tenhune and makers of old movies.<p>The wild and crazy romp with the supernatural begins on October 1 and ends....fittingly....on All Hallows Eve, and besides the thrashing Jack, you'll encounter favorites like Dracula, Dr. Frankenstein, Sherlock Holmes and other creatures of the night lurking about in the nearby woods and graveyards.</p><p>Great read....Great book-cover....Loved every minute of it!</p></span>

<div id="review_60007192" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

    <a title="Jim" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/695116-jim"><img alt="Jim" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1340192527p2/695116.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer60007192" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2035982489973605141">Oct2017: Reading yet again with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/topic/show/18938021' rel='nofollow noopener'>Fantasy Book Club</a>. Many thanks to Helen for inviting me to read along. It is in memory of Brenda who recently lost a battle to cancer & this was one of her favorite books. Mine too, obviously. Definitely a Halloween tradition. I must watch "The Rocky Horror Picture Show" tonight. The one with Tim Curry, of course.<br/><br/>It was a great read with a great bunch of people. I added some to my notes & we relabeled the characters on the front cover due to a great insight by Ann</span>
  <span id="freeText2035982489973605141" style="display:none">Oct2017: Reading yet again with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/topic/show/18938021" rel="nofollow noopener">Fantasy Book Club</a>. Many thanks to Helen for inviting me to read along. It is in memory of Brenda who recently lost a battle to cancer &amp; this was one of her favorite books. Mine too, obviously. Definitely a Halloween tradition. I must watch "The Rocky Horror Picture Show" tonight. The one with Tim Curry, of course.<br /><br />It was a great read with a great bunch of people. I added some to my notes &amp; we relabeled the characters on the front cover due to a great insight by Anna. She saw the characters as grouped by their roles in the story. That's a major spoiler, so don't look until you've read the book, but it makes so much sense. It leaves the Great Detective unaccounted for &amp; possibly one extra character on the far left. My guess is he is disguised as the waiter &amp; the Inspector is peeking in.<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/photo/group/22645-roger-zelazny?page=1&amp;photo=3638171">https://www.goodreads.com/photo/group...</a><br /><br />James Warhola finally looked through his old boxes (6 years of nagging!) &amp; found the folder for this book. No notes, but he did find some sketches. There are 5 of them posted in the Zelazny group's photos here:<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/photo/group/22645-roger-zelazny">https://www.goodreads.com/photo/group...</a><br /><br />Oct2011: I made up a set of notes this year from discussions over the past couple of years in the Roger Zelazny group here:<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/topic/show/218652">http://www.goodreads.com/topic/show/2...</a><br /><br />This year we discussed the cover art &amp; I even traded some emails with James Warhola. Hopefully he'll remember to look up his notes &amp; fill me in on who is who. While some of the characters are obvious, several are not. Here's the full picture, much of which is cut out on the cover:<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.full-wallpaper.com/affiche.php?a=art&amp;b=Gladius-One&amp;c=Gladius_0093_James_Warhola_A_Night_in_the_Lonesome_October.jpg">http://www.full-wallpaper.com/affiche...</a><br /><br />As always, it was a very enjoyable read &amp; I actually managed to limit myself to one chapter a day. I picked up a few more tidbits this year, which is pretty amazing. As fun as it is to read just the obvious story, the subtleties make it even better.<br /><br />Oct2009: What a fantastic read for October, especially if done one day at a time while discussing with others. That allows plenty of time for reflection on the various clues, trying to figure out who the characters are &amp; what the Game is about. <br /><br />The book is a 'lunatic scavenger hunt' drawing characters &amp; the setting from a lot of classical sources. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/9494.H_P__Lovecraft" title="H.P. Lovecraft" rel="nofollow noopener">H.P. Lovecraft</a>'s Cthulhu myths are a core component with players mostly from Victorian England classics; Jack the Ripper, Sherlock Holmes, Victor Frankenstein, Dracula &amp; more. Few are named directly &amp; some are tough to figure out, but it makes for a very fun read.<br /><br />We summarized the book, one day at a time, discussing the characters, their names &amp; more about the book in the Roger Zelazny group in the spoiler topic.<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/topic/show/218652-a-night-in-the-lonesome-october-spoilers">http://www.goodreads.com/topic/show/2...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="2035982489973605141" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Celeste" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Celeste" href="/user/show/7317186-celeste">Celeste</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7317186-celeste?shelf=funny">funny</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7317186-celeste?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7317186-celeste?shelf=spooky">spooky</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2140693899" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6516896389967567478">Actual rating: 3.5<br/><br/>I actually managed to stick to the one chapter a day format of this book, which made for a fun little adventure. <br/><br/>This is the second Zelazny novel I’ve read, having only dipped my toe into his Chronicles of Amber with the first book. Zelazny is a science fiction and fantasy forefather of the 1960s through the 1980s, having influenced the likes of Neil Gaiman and George R.R. Martin. He won 3 Nebula Awards and 6 Hugo Awards, and is most famous for his Chronicles of Amber. In other</span>
  <span id="freeText6516896389967567478" style="display:none">Actual rating: 3.5<br /><br />I actually managed to stick to the one chapter a day format of this book, which made for a fun little adventure. <br /><br />This is the second Zelazny novel I’ve read, having only dipped my toe into his Chronicles of Amber with the first book. Zelazny is a science fiction and fantasy forefather of the 1960s through the 1980s, having influenced the likes of Neil Gaiman and George R.R. Martin. He won 3 Nebula Awards and 6 Hugo Awards, and is most famous for his Chronicles of Amber. In other words, we have him to thank for some of the stories and authors that we as SFF fans love so much.<br /><br />I didn’t love this little book, but I liked it. The aforementioned format was engaging and unique, and the plot was very original. But those were honestly my two favorite aspects of the book. Snuff, our canine narrator, was an entertaining and charming, and the Game he was involved in remained mysterious even at the novel’s end. All of the players were well known characters or tropes from classic horror fiction, which added to the fun factor. For a Game that had a possibly apocalyptic outcome, the way the story was told seemed very slice-of-life, which removed some of the tension needed to fully absorb a reader in a cosmic conflict. <br /><br />A Night in the Lonesome October was a light October read, perfect for getting into the spirit of the season. It just left me wanting a bit more. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6516896389967567478" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer15055645764023918748">3.5 <br/><br/>I'm a Universal Monster nut. I have the stuffed animal collection, the silver screen box, key chains, artwork for the poster of The Creature from the Black Lagoon signed by the artist (and autographs from Ricou Browning and Julie Adams from a convention on it years later), a few other collectables, the collector box set with statues of Dracula, Frankenstein and The Wolf Man...I'd have much more but, you know, I'm poor.<br/><br/>This book gets brownie points just for including some of these characters.</span>
  <span id="freeText15055645764023918748" style="display:none">3.5 <br /><br />I'm a Universal Monster nut. I have the stuffed animal collection, the silver screen box, key chains, artwork for the poster of The Creature from the Black Lagoon signed by the artist (and autographs from Ricou Browning and Julie Adams from a convention on it years later), a few other collectables, the collector box set with statues of Dracula, Frankenstein and The Wolf Man...I'd have much more but, you know, I'm poor.<br /><br />This book gets brownie points just for including some of these characters. My heart went aflutter seeing the names Count and Larry Talbot. Being told through the points of view of the animals was just another cherry on top of the fandom-sundae.<br /><br />It's a quick read with odd artwork. Not a children's tale because of the language and content, but parts of it read like one. I think it's because it's capturing the magic of youth and adulthood all in one, something we never really outgrow.<br /><br />Despite how much I loved about the book, my enjoyment comes to a 3.5 star rating. Not to sound dense, but some of the story confused me to tears and there were some dragging bits. I did dig the twist at the end with the count and also loved Jack and his scenes of saving his faithful hound.<br /><br />Recommended for everyone - Halloween or any time of the year, young or old.</span>

<div id="review_1606278722" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1606278722?book_show_action=true">Oct 23, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Layla ✷ Praise the sun ✷" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Layla ✷ Praise the sun ✷" href="/user/show/45487389-layla-praise-the-sun">Layla ✷ Praise the sun ✷</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

      <a href="/user/show/9340136-evgeny">Evgeny</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1606278722" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2754066313609082410">Halloween buddy read with some of my awesome goodreads friends.<br/><br/><i>
  <b>Growing moon. Angry cat. Feather in the wind. <br/>Autumn comes. The grass dies.</b>
</i> <br/><br/>"A Night in the Lonesome October" is <i>
  <b>a very different book in so many ways. In so many good ways</b>
</i>. <br/><br/>It is written from a dog's point of view and consists of a prologue plus 31 chapters, one chapter for each day of October. <br/><br/>You have no idea what is going on in the major part of the book, but instead you come across all sorts of characters that you might </span>
  <span id="freeText2754066313609082410" style="display:none">Halloween buddy read with some of my awesome goodreads friends.<br><br><i>
  <b>Growing moon. Angry cat. Feather in the wind. <br>Autumn comes. The grass dies.</b>
</i> <br><br>"A Night in the Lonesome October" is <i>
  <b>a very different book in so many ways. In so many good ways</b>
</i>. <br><br>It is written from a dog's point of view and consists of a prologue plus 31 chapters, one chapter for each day of October. <br><br>You have no idea what is going on in the major part of the book, but instead you come across all sorts of characters that you might for instance know from other books or the real world (Jack the Ripper says hi is all I'll say) as you gather hints and clues as to what exactly is happening here. <br><br>Many of those hints are so subtle, it's simply brilliant, which is why I will not say more about the plot here. It would already give away way too much. <br><br>While the book is a quick read and seems rather light and funny on the surface, it is really pretty creepy and touches upon topics such as vivisection, murder and grave-robbing. At times it feels surrealistic, other times it is poetic and heartbreaking, too. <br><br><i>
  <b>He cared about people, about the whole world. What’s that human notion—compassion. He had a lot of that. It’s one of the reasons he drank a lot, I think. He felt everybody else’s pain too much.</b>
</i><br><br>In short, it makes you feel all the feels - if you let it do so. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1508952470i/24270947.jpg" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>
  <b>I felt a strong desire to howl at the moon. It was such a howlable moon.</b>
</i><br><br>I feel that I could never do a book such as this credit with my limited ability to express myself by writing a review for it, so I will leave it to you now to pick it up and see for yourself, because you definitely should. <br><br>Last, but not least, thank you, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/9340136-evgeny" rel="nofollow noopener">Evgeny</a>, for drawing this book to my attention, and for the hints you gave us. I would have missed so many of them had it not been for you.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2754066313609082410" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2907942439" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2907942439" />
    <a title="Juho Pohjalainen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/85347537-juho-pohjalainen"><img alt="Juho Pohjalainen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1555446239p2/85347537.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2907942439?book_show_action=true">Jul 28, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Juho Pohjalainen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Juho Pohjalainen" href="/user/show/85347537-juho-pohjalainen">Juho Pohjalainen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2907942439" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11759966598945617940">This book throws you right in the middle of bizarre events full of wizards and talking animals and moon stuff, forced to scramble on your feet and pick up your bearings with little to no exposition, almost as if you were a part of the Game they were all playing as well. Gradually it sets up as a high-stakes crossover conflict involving well-known public domain characters fighting off (or helping out) eldritch abominations from beyond this earth. It's like trying to build a thousand-piece puzzle </span>
  <span id="freeText11759966598945617940" style="display:none">This book throws you right in the middle of bizarre events full of wizards and talking animals and moon stuff, forced to scramble on your feet and pick up your bearings with little to no exposition, almost as if you were a part of the Game they were all playing as well. Gradually it sets up as a high-stakes crossover conflict involving well-known public domain characters fighting off (or helping out) eldritch abominations from beyond this earth. It's like trying to build a thousand-piece puzzle with no image to help, but bit by bit it reveals itself to be a grand and beautiful work of art.<br /><br />The narrative voice is terse but effective, as it always is with Zelazny, and the characters involved are all a curious and reasonably well-developed folk that I wouldn't have previously imagined myself to root for. But I do still think that it could've used to set up the scene and the conflict a little bit more from the beginning, and by the same token, it ended rather abruptly as well.<br /><br />But those are quibbles. On the whole, it was a fun quick read.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11759966598945617940" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">for Halloween</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer9993962" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15043374397177545787">This amalgamation of Victorian gothic and penny dreadful cliches is the best example of Zelazny's tongue-in-cheek humor. Without taking itself too seriously, the book avoids the campiness of the author's <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/239922.Bring_Me_the_Head_of_Prince_Charming__Millennial_Contest_1_' title='Bring Me the Head of Prince Charming (Millennial Contest 1) by Roger Zelazny' rel='nofollow noopener'>Bring Me the Head of Prince Charming</a> and manages to be exciting and plot-driven without losing its sense of whimsy. Zelazny also succeeds in capturing the requisite dark-and-shadowed-Victorian-London atmosphere without becoming unbearably heavy or going to extremes of nastiness, as many recent u</span>
  <span id="freeText15043374397177545787" style="display:none">This amalgamation of Victorian gothic and penny dreadful cliches is the best example of Zelazny's tongue-in-cheek humor. Without taking itself too seriously, the book avoids the campiness of the author's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/239922.Bring_Me_the_Head_of_Prince_Charming__Millennial_Contest_1_" title="Bring Me the Head of Prince Charming (Millennial Contest 1) by Roger Zelazny" rel="nofollow noopener">Bring Me the Head of Prince Charming</a> and manages to be exciting and plot-driven without losing its sense of whimsy. Zelazny also succeeds in capturing the requisite dark-and-shadowed-Victorian-London atmosphere without becoming unbearably heavy or going to extremes of nastiness, as many recent users of Victorian settings seem driven to do.</span>

<div id="review_1418224106" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1418224106" />
    <a title="William" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/997203-william"><img alt="William" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1529787483p2/997203.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1418224106?book_show_action=true">Oct 16, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="William" class="user" itemprop="url" name="William" href="/user/show/997203-william">William</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1418224106" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12444364053337069036">A wonderful book in every sense of the word, and perfect October reading. Jack the Ripper, the Wolfman, Sherlock Holmes, Dr Frankenstein ( and his monster), Dracula, a witch, a mad monk, an evil vicar and many more, all attempting to perform a ritual to either allow Lovecraftian old ones through to our plane, or prevent it from happening. And all ably narrated by Snuff, Jack's faithful, and possibly immortal, dog companion. Zelazny was on top form here, a towering talent, taken far too early.<br/><br/>It'</span>
  <span id="freeText12444364053337069036" style="display:none">A wonderful book in every sense of the word, and perfect October reading. Jack the Ripper, the Wolfman, Sherlock Holmes, Dr Frankenstein ( and his monster), Dracula, a witch, a mad monk, an evil vicar and many more, all attempting to perform a ritual to either allow Lovecraftian old ones through to our plane, or prevent it from happening. And all ably narrated by Snuff, Jack's faithful, and possibly immortal, dog companion. Zelazny was on top form here, a towering talent, taken far too early.<br /><br />It's gorgeously written, humorous, completely immersive and one of the greatest things since sliced bread. Do yourself a favor and get onto this straight away - you can thank me later.<br /><br />And try to get the illustrated version - the b&amp;W drawings accompanying the text complement it perfectly.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_76118734" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/76118734" />
    <a title=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books"><img alt=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1403239075p2/1570669.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/76118734?book_show_action=true">Oct 29, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" class="user" itemprop="url" name=" Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)" href="/user/show/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books"> Danielle The Book Huntress (Back to the Books)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fans of the classic horror movie characters</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=famous-literary-historical-characte">famous-literary-historical-characte</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=humor">humor</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=witch-sorcereress-healer">witch-sorcereress-healer</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=wizard-warlock-sorcerer">wizard-warlock-sorcerer</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=library-checkout">library-checkout</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=animal-centered-fiction">animal-centered-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=animal-character-steals-the-show">animal-character-steals-the-show</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=humorous-fantasy">humorous-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=old-school-horror">old-school-horror</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1570669-danielle-the-book-huntress-back-to-the-books?shelf=pastiche-send-up-homage">pastiche-send-up-homage</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer76118734" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3955479386436155578">Goodness gracious, I am super late writing this review. My schedule just exploded after the middle of October, and I had no time. Because it's been nearly a month, I don't have the best memory of all the plotlines. But I promised I would write a review for every book I read, so better late than never, and my review will be of the more general sort.<br/><br/>I was fortunate to find this at my library and it fit very well thematically into my October Scare Fest reading. I enjoyed it overall. It's an odd lit</span>
  <span id="freeText3955479386436155578" style="display:none">Goodness gracious, I am super late writing this review. My schedule just exploded after the middle of October, and I had no time. Because it's been nearly a month, I don't have the best memory of all the plotlines. But I promised I would write a review for every book I read, so better late than never, and my review will be of the more general sort.<br /><br />I was fortunate to find this at my library and it fit very well thematically into my October Scare Fest reading. I enjoyed it overall. It's an odd little book, no question about it. I would consider it a bit of a pastiche to the famous literary figures of Dracula, Frankenstein and his monster, Sherlock Holmes, Merlin-type druids, and the Wolfman. I rather enjoyed that about this book. What I loved the most is that the narrators are the familiars, or animal companions of the human (or humanlike characters). They all strike up a strange sort of friendship driven by mutual interest and that old adage that drives too many middle grade friendships, especially among girls: better to be friends with someone than to have them as an enemy. <br /><br />The story's chapters are broken down into each one representing a day in October. They are getting ready for some very important magical event that will have seemingly profound consequences. It sort of reminded me of the Highlander movie where the various characters are pairing off against each other, but this was more of a semi-good versus evil sort of standoff. Just my take. Forgive me if I am way off here. I didn't quite understand all of that, but I don't think it was as important as the unfolding paranormal mystery as various human (or humanlike) characters start to be picked off, one by one. The main character is a dog, who is the familiar of a male wizard. He's an endearing narrator. I liked how he plays dumb dog when necessary, but he's not the average canine (I truly feel some dogs are incredibly intelligent, so don't assume I'm picking on dogs here). I liked his wry and atypical friendship with a cat, who is the familiar of a witch. Along with the fact that their humans are striking up a courtship that may not end well if they end up choosing opposite sides. There is also a bat, rat, snake, and owl character. I'm sorry I don't remember all their names. I do remember the snake's name was Quicklime, so go figure. Strangely enough, the humanlike character who was most developed was Larry Talbot. Classic horror movie buffs will recognize that name as that of the Wolf Man. He did have the tragic vibe of the character in the movie, but he was quite likable.<br /><br />This book isn't that deep. I mean it's a short book and probably has some hidden meaning, and I think a very prominent satirical tone that some readers will pick up on immediately. It's not super scary, it's a bit. Enough to make for a nice Halloween read. <br /><br />I'd say this one is worth tracking down if you can find it at your library. Unfortunately, it's out of print. <br /><br />A good read for this time of year. And fun for animal lovers like myself.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3955479386436155578" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_66886405" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/66886405" />
    <a title="Chris " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1956959-chris"><img alt="Chris " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1502408626p2/1956959.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/66886405?book_show_action=true">Aug 10, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chris " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chris " href="/user/show/1956959-chris">Chris </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780688125080" href="/book/show/737453.A_Night_in_the_Lonesome_October">review of another edition</a>


          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Chris  by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/695116-jim">Jim</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1956959-chris?shelf=scifi-fan-group">scifi-fan-group</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1956959-chris?shelf=read-owned-hardcover">read-owned-hardcover</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1956959-chris?shelf=zelazny-group">zelazny-group</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer66886405" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12508125867895272077">A very enjoyable read from <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3619.Roger_Zelazny' title='Roger Zelazny' rel='nofollow noopener'>Roger Zelazny</a>, consistent with other material I've read by him.<br/><br/>The tone is light, although the subject matter is grim. It seems that on Halloween night, unimaginable horrors will attempt to enter this world. A gathering of powers has come together, some to hold it back, and some to try to help it along.<br/><br/>Throughout the month, these opposing forces are playing a game of positioning, alliances, and grabs for talismans to help their cause or hinder the opposition.<br/><br/>The story </span>
  <span id="freeText12508125867895272077" style="display:none">A very enjoyable read from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3619.Roger_Zelazny" title="Roger Zelazny" rel="nofollow noopener">Roger Zelazny</a>, consistent with other material I've read by him.<br /><br />The tone is light, although the subject matter is grim. It seems that on Halloween night, unimaginable horrors will attempt to enter this world. A gathering of powers has come together, some to hold it back, and some to try to help it along.<br /><br />Throughout the month, these opposing forces are playing a game of positioning, alliances, and grabs for talismans to help their cause or hinder the opposition.<br /><br />The story is told by Snuff, the trusty dog of Jack the Ripper. He interacts with other players in the game, and the animal companions of these players. We get cameo appearances from major characters of horror stories written in the 1800's, or from movies about stories in that era.<br /><br />This came out as a nice mix of horror and comedy, intrigue and mystery, and a puzzle for the reader to pick up on all the outside references.<br /><br />The chapters are broken down to 31, one for each day of October. I read this one chapter a day for the month, along with some good friends, to experience the story as Snuff pretty much lived it.<br /><br />I think this is one that could be read again, perhaps as early as next October, when the weather is changing, it's getting dark earlier, and there is a crispness in the air. It's a perfect mood book for the season, and I think there are little tidbits that will be picked up in subsequent readings. <br /><br />We'll see. Watch for an update in October of 2011. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12508125867895272077" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_217380084" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/217380084" />
    <a title="Becky" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1376766-becky"><img alt="Becky" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582132250p2/1376766.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/217380084?book_show_action=true">Sep 30, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Becky" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Becky" href="/user/show/1376766-becky">Becky</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=multi-dimensional">multi-dimensional</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=vampires">vampires</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=mystery-and-thrillers">mystery-and-thrillers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=2011">2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=ebook_nook">ebook_nook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1376766-becky?shelf=mythology">mythology</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer217380084" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9017305796489943015">This was my second attempt at reading Zelazny, and although I enjoyed this one more than the last one, I am beginning to think that Zelazny's style just doesn't agree with me. <br/><br/>The best way that I can think to describe it is that I feel like I'm seeing the events of the story out of the corner of my eye, that I can never quite get the full picture. We're given hints, references to puzzle out, dialogue that both reveals and obscures, and a narration that is restrained and secretive. Everything is </span>
  <span id="freeText9017305796489943015" style="display:none">This was my second attempt at reading Zelazny, and although I enjoyed this one more than the last one, I am beginning to think that Zelazny's style just doesn't agree with me. <br /><br />The best way that I can think to describe it is that I feel like I'm seeing the events of the story out of the corner of my eye, that I can never quite get the full picture. We're given hints, references to puzzle out, dialogue that both reveals and obscures, and a narration that is restrained and secretive. Everything is parceled out in small increments of info... a hint here, a clue there, which matches the fact that most of the characters are also figuring it out, but there is knowledge and history that our narrator has but doesn't share with us. At the same time, we're just thrown into it and expected to either sink or swim, get it or don't, or just go with it and hope it makes sense by the end. <br /><br />This is really frustrating for me, because I want to be drawn into the story and live in it a little while and just enjoy it for what it is. But Zelazny's style, in both this story and the previous one I read, requires the reader's having external knowledge in order to understand what's going on. The previous one required quite a bit of classical Greek history and mythology knowledge, and this one requires quite a bit of classic mystery and/or horror and lore knowledge as well. If one is not a classic reader, they will not get or understand many of the references here. And there are MANY, MANY references to be found. I have read many of the classics referred to, and I still felt like... well, like I could only see part of the picture. <br /><br />I'm sure that this kind of style works for a lot of people, especially those who like to puzzle things out and find those little Easter Eggs and such. And usually, I am that type. I like stories that don't give up all of their secrets all at once, that allow you to find something new with each reading. It's one of the things that I loved about the Harry Potter series, seeing all the mythological and historical references and figuring them out and trying to see if they signified anything that was to come in the main storyline. But the difference, at least as I see it, is that even if one didn't see those references at all in Harry Potter, there was a story to be enjoyed anyway. The characters were well developed on their own, the history was provided, and we knew what was going on, and the storyline made sense without needing to know that Albus means "white", etc. In a story like Harry Potter, those references are like the edible glitter on top of the icing of a cake. They add depth and something special... but without them, you still have a damn delicious cake. <br /><br />I don't feel like that was the case here. I got quite a lot of the references, because I HAVE read many of the books hinted at, and have at least a semi-passing knowledge of other types of lore, but I know that were I to have more knowledge, I would have enjoyed this story more. I have nothing against Zelazny, but I do feel like he kind of has an "ideal audience" in mind for his stories. I'm just probably not in it. <br /><br />Anyway, I did like this story, after I hit the halfway mark and the chapters got longer than 1 or 2 pages. I did like the references to the classics, and enjoyed the overall concept itself. I liked the Lovecraftian feel of the Things and the slitherers, and the 'through the stones' section. I liked how the mystery kept building up, but I would have liked for the resolution to be more complete and explained. <br /><br />Overall, I thought the story was good, but I would have liked it to be more fleshed out as a whole. I'm glad that I read it, it's a good Halloweenish story, but giving a bit more background and filler knowledge would have benefited it, I think. <br /><br />Horror October 2011: #6</span>
  <a data-text-id="9017305796489943015" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Stepheny" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7091879-stepheny"><img alt="Stepheny" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1567725280p2/7091879.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1046276627?book_show_action=true">Sep 05, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stepheny" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stepheny" href="/user/show/7091879-stepheny">Stepheny</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1046276627" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7413013915600876015">3.5 <br/><br/>I read A Night in the Lonesome October with some of my favorite gal pals on goodreads. I wasn’t quite sure what to expect but what I got was not at all what I had imagined.<br/><br/>The story is told in 31 chapters- each one is a day in October. You are following around Snuff, a watchdog who tells you all about his adventures for the day. There are other animals that are in the story as well working with their human companion to collect items and information for what they refer to as “The Game”. <br/><br/>Imagi</span>
  <span id="freeText7413013915600876015" style="display:none">3.5 <br /><br />I read A Night in the Lonesome October with some of my favorite gal pals on goodreads. I wasn’t quite sure what to expect but what I got was not at all what I had imagined.<br /><br />The story is told in 31 chapters- each one is a day in October. You are following around Snuff, a watchdog who tells you all about his adventures for the day. There are other animals that are in the story as well working with their human companion to collect items and information for what they refer to as “The Game”. <br /><br />Imagine going to a movie theater and sitting down in your seat with your supersized popcorn, box of milk duds and your $18 bottle of water only to find you forgot your glasses in the car. (I don’t wear glasses either, but just go along with it for a minute and pretend your eyes suck). You’re all cozy, everyone is gathered in to watch the movie. You don’t want to be the jerk that gets up and interrupts everyone to ask what the hell is going on, or that blocks the view for someone else so you sit patiently hoping you can figure out enough from the dialogue. With 15 minutes left in the movie you decide to reach in your bag and get your keys out so you can try to beat the rush. Upon reaching in your bag you find your damn glasses. Sure, it’s great that you can NOW see the movie, but most of it has been lost in a haze. <br /><br />That’s exactly how I feel about this book. I don’t know if I am too dumb to pick up on all of the references but apparently everyone else who read this book figured out that Snuff was Jack the Ripper’s dog. I never made that connection and we can blame that on my blonde roots I guess. <br /><br />Overall I enjoyed the story. I mostly loved the kitty because I love kitties. The friendship between the animals, even ones who were on opposing sides of “The Game” was truly great. I felt like I missed a lot in this book though and I’m not quite sure why. Maybe it’s me or my ignorance of historical references? Maybe it’s the subtle writing technique that Mr. Zelazny employed? Maybe a combination of both? <br /><br />Once I got to the ending and realized what “the Game” actually was, it helped clear up some of the fog that had blocked my view. But not all of it. I’ll most likely go back at some point, maybe on a lonesome night in October, and give it another shot now that it’s all been spelled out for me. I want to thank my Goodreads Gal Pals for encouraging me to try new things and especially thanks to Delee for choosing this particular book. It was such a fun read even though I wasn’t smart enough to pick up on all the references! <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7413013915600876015" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('v2sG3ykmzsma/2B4Erzb4k9JaF7IOol5mMgoaesVVxGVgnfJJ+OH2gujvOQuBbhDmLeoEj3hTTbKtNMjAhjXLg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  }

У кожної з восьми фігур є своя історія, своя тінь на пожовклій від часу стіні. Навіщо літнє подружжя прямує у самісіньке серце небезпечної зони Темряви? Що ховається за личиною гротескного «ми»? Як утекти від потойбічного птаха, якщо він оселився у твоїй голові? Хто переможе у протистоянні між Китом, Островом і Темрявою? Чи можна знайти Бога? І, зрештою, де не ходить смерть?\n\nНизка символів, що проходить крізь усі частини книжки, поступово перетворюється на тло для прихованої, дев’ятої історії, де поєднуються всі події, всі сенси та натяки. І тоді вам буде що сказати чорній істоті з зубастою пащею, яка чекає наприкінці шляху.\n\nЦі тексти химерні. Приховані знаки – підступні. Силуети за поворотом – жаскі. Зазвичай автор проводить гостей манівцями, підготовленими заздалегідь, аби зрештою розповісти свою історію. Що ж, не цього разу. Євген Лір випускає з підвалів своєї свідомості темних псів, самогубців, шукачів метафізичних істин і навіть художницю-криміналістку, аби ті сплелися у потойбічному танці навколо мерехтливої свічки – уяви свого читача – і змусили його віднайти свій шлях самотужки. Подорож світом цієї збірки небезпечна, але від цього ще захопливіша. Вісім оповідань, що увійшли до книжки, тісно пов’язані між собою символами, подіями та натяками. І якщо вам стане снаги поєднати знаки під правильним кутом, ви отримаєте дев’яту історію, приховану під опалим листям, – бо найцікавіше завжди приховане від очей.\n\nПрислухайтесь. Чуєте?       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/3619.Roger_Zelazny">About Roger Zelazny</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/3619.Roger_Zelazny"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1207671346p3/3619.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/3619.Roger_Zelazny">Roger Zelazny
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
3,062
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer17940690605242720101">Roger Zelazny made his name with a group of novellas which demonstrated just how intense an emotional charge could be generated by the stock imagery of sf; the most famous of these is <i>A Rose for Ecclesiastes</i> in which a poet struggles to convince dying and sterile Martians that life is worth continuing. Zelazny continued to write excellent short stories throughout his career. Most of his novels dea</span>
  <span id="freeText17940690605242720101" style="display:none">Roger Zelazny made his name with a group of novellas which demonstrated just how intense an emotional charge could be generated by the stock imagery of sf; the most famous of these is <i>A Rose for Ecclesiastes</i> in which a poet struggles to convince dying and sterile Martians that life is worth continuing. Zelazny continued to write excellent short stories throughout his career. Most of his novels deal, one way or another, with tricksters and mythology, often with rogues who become gods, like Sam in <i>Lord of Light</i>, who reinvents Buddhism as a vehicle for political subversion on a colony planet.<br /><br />The fantasy sequence <i>The Amber Chronicles</i>, which started with <i>Nine Princes in Amber</i>, deals with the ruling family of a Platonic realm at the metaphysical heart of things, who can slide, trickster-like through realities, and their wars with each other and the related ruling house of Chaos. Zelazny never entirely fulfilled his early promise—who could?—but he and his work were much loved, and a potent influence on such younger writers as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/346732.George_R__R__Martin" title="George R. R. Martin" rel="nofollow noopener">George R. R. Martin</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1221698.Neil_Gaiman" title="Neil Gaiman" rel="nofollow noopener">Neil Gaiman</a>.<br /><br />He won the Nebula award three times (out of 14 nominations) and the Hugo award six times (out of 14 nominations). His <a href="http://aok.lib.umbc.edu/specoll/Zelazny/index.php" rel="nofollow noopener">papers are housed</a> at the Albin O. Khun Library of the University of Maryland, Baltimore County (UMBC).<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roger_Zelazny">http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roger_Ze...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="17940690605242720101" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>
